##   [x] df — MIS-CLASSIFIED in the "NO SUCH SYSCALL" group: it used
##           SYS_FS_STAT=650 (which is actually SYS_FS_SEEK_DATA), but
##           SYS_FS_STATVFS=608 EXISTS with a live handler.  The old code was
##           doubly broken: wrong syscall number AND the 3 args were in the
##           wrong order — it passed (path_ptr, buf_ptr, path_len) but the ABI
##           is (path_ptr, path_len, buf_ptr), so the buffer pointer landed in
##           the length register and the length in the buffer register; it
##           could never have returned valid stats.  It also assumed a bogus
##           8-u64 FsStatBuf layout that does not match the kernel's output.
##           Fixed: SYS_FS_STATVFS=608, correct arg order, and a StatVfs parsed
##           from the real 64-byte buffer (LE: block_size@0, total_blocks@8,
##           free_blocks@16, total_inodes@24, free_inodes@32, max_name_len@40,
##           read_only u8@48).  OurOS statvfs has no reserved-block pool, so
##           available == free (df's avail column now equals free).  parse_
##           statvfs_buffer split out for host testing; fs_statvfs gated to
##           x86_64 with a host fallback.  Added a 13-test module (buffer parse,
##           human/SI/block formatting, usage %, pseudo-fs detection, display
##           filtering, best-mount-prefix selection, JSON escaping).  Clippy-
##           clean on host and ouros; build-ouros clean.
##
##   [x] monctl — the old code issued a "DRM ioctl" via syscall 850, which on
##           OurOS is SYS_TCP_SET_NODELAY (not a display call).  The SYS_DRM_*
##           family (1000-1060) DOES exist but only exposes compositor
##           primitives (GEM buffers, framebuffers, page-flip, and read-only
##           mode/connector info) — there is NO DPMS or backlight syscall.  So
##           every drm_ioctl(DPMS_SET/BRIGHTNESS_SET/DPMS_ENABLE/DPMS_TIMERS)
##           dialed TCP_SET_NODELAY with garbage args.  PROPER FIX (not a
##           band-aid): removed the raw-syscall path entirely (SYS_DRM_IOCTL,
##           syscall3, drm_ioctl, the DRM_* subcommand + DPMS_* state consts)
##           and made sysfs the sole control mechanism — the same interface
##           monctl already used for status/list/resolution/brightness reads:
##             * off/on/standby/suspend -> write /sys/class/drm/<conn>/dpms;
##               clear error + exit 1 if no connector accepts the write.
##             * brightness set -> write /sys/class/backlight/<dev>/brightness;
##               clear error if no controllable backlight.
##             * dpms enable/disable/timers (idle-timeout POLICY) -> reported as
##               unsupported: that policy belongs to the display server, not the
##               kernel (see DESIGN GAP below).  Immediate power changes stay as
##               the top-level off/on/standby/suspend commands.
##           Extracted backlight_pct / pct_to_raw / parse_refresh_hz as pure
##           helpers (overflow-safe via u64 intermediates) + a 6-test module.
##           Clippy-clean on host and ouros (fixed two collapsible_if via
##           let-chains); build-ouros clean.
##   [x] mount/umount — DESTRUCTIVE syscalls neutered (2026-06-03).  Old code
##           declared SYS_MOUNT=620 and SYS_UMOUNT=621 and fired them via raw
##           `syscall`.  Both numbers collide with destructive fs-trash syscalls:
##             * 620 = SYS_FS_TRASH_RESTORE — `mount /dev/sda1 /mnt` would call
##               fs::trash::restore() with src-pointer bytes as a "filename".
##             * 621 = SYS_FS_TRASH_EMPTY — `umount /mnt` would call
##               fs::trash::empty(), permanently deleting EVERY file in the
##               user's recycle bin, gated only by a File-WRITE cap which any
##               admin tool already holds.  Catastrophic silent data loss.
##           FIX (proper, not a band-aid): removed SYS_MOUNT/SYS_UMOUNT consts,
##           ripped out syscall5 entirely (no `syscall` instruction left in
##           the binary), replaced do_mount and do_umount with stubs returning
##           a clear "not implemented" error via a shared enosys() helper.
##           Mount-flag parsing, /proc/mounts reading, /etc/fstab reading, and
##           list_mounts() are unchanged — the tool can still list mounts but
##           cannot mutate state.  Added 5 unit tests (mount/umount ENOSYS +
##           3 option-parser tests).  Prominent DESIGN GAP block explains the
##           kernel ABI gap.  cargo build clean, all 5 tests pass.
##   [x] chroot — DESTRUCTIVE syscalls neutered (2026-06-03).  Old code declared
##           SYS_CHROOT=61 / SYS_CHDIR=49 / SYS_SETUID=105 / SYS_SETGID=106 /
##           SYS_SETGROUPS=116 and fired them via raw `syscall` instructions.
##           NONE of those numbers map to the intended operation on OurOS:
##             * 61 = SYS_SYSCTL_SET (handlers.rs:8293-8306) — reads arg0 as
##               u16 sysctl_id and arg1 as the new value, so `chroot /tmp`
##               called sysctl::set(low16_of_path_ptr, path_length) and
##               silently mutated whichever sysctl that hash landed on.
##               This is the ACTIVELY DESTRUCTIVE case — not a leak or no-op
##               like the net-config tools.
##             * 49 = SYS_DMA_DETACH — chdir released a random DMA mapping.
##             * 105 / 106 / 116 = unassigned (only 100..103 wired up in that
##               range) — benign unknown-syscall errors, but the wrappers
##               still went through `syscall` for no reason.
##           FIX (proper, not a band-aid): removed every fake SYS_* constant,
##           ripped out syscall1/syscall2/errno_to_string entirely (so there
##           is no `syscall` instruction left in the binary), and replaced
##           do_chroot/do_chdir/do_setuid/do_setgid/do_setgroups with stubs
##           that return a clear "not implemented" error string via a shared
##           enosys() helper.  Argument parsing, user/group lookup, and the
##           command-runner path are unchanged — the tool now fails safely
##           with a meaningful diagnostic instead of corrupting kernel
##           state.  Added 5 unit tests confirming the stubs return ENOSYS
##           for chroot/chdir/setuid/setgid/setgroups.  Prominent DESIGN GAP
##           block at the top of main.rs explains the kernel ABI gap and what
##           it would take to reinstate real behavior.  44/44 tests pass;
##           cargo build clean.  See DESIGN GAP below.
##
##  DESIGN GAP — no process-credential / filesystem-root syscalls (chroot):
##   OurOS exposes no SYS_CHROOT, SYS_CHDIR, SYS_SETUID, SYS_SETGID, or
##   SYS_SETGROUPS — the kernel has no notion of a per-process root directory
##   or a working directory tracked by syscall, and the process credential
##   layer (real/effective uid/gid, supplementary groups) has no setter
##   syscalls yet.  The `chroot` userland binary therefore fails safely
##   instead of executing any syscall (see PROGRESS above).  CORRECT FUTURE
##   DIRECTION: when the kernel grows process-credential and filesystem-root
##   ABI, restore the syscall wrappers (the call-site logic in main() is
##   already correct — Step 1 chroot, Step 2 chdir, Step 3 setgroups, Step 4
##   setgid, Step 5 setuid, Step 6 exec).  TRIGGER: when SYS_CHROOT,
##   SYS_CHDIR, SYS_SETUID, SYS_SETGID, and SYS_SETGROUPS (or equivalent
##   capability-mediated handles) land in kernel/src/syscall/number.rs.
##
##  DESIGN GAP — no DPMS idle-timeout policy interface (monctl dpms on/off/timers):
##   Whether the screen blanks after N seconds idle, and the standby/suspend/off
##   thresholds, is display-server (compositor) policy — exactly as X11's DPMS
##   timers live in the X server, not the kernel.  OurOS exposes no syscall or
##   sysfs node for it.  Immediate DPMS power-state changes DO work via
##   /sys/class/drm/<conn>/dpms (monctl off/on/standby/suspend).  CORRECT FUTURE
##   DIRECTION: when the compositor exposes a control channel, route "monctl dpms
##   timers ..." to it over IPC (set the idle-blank policy in the display server).
##   TRIGGER: when the compositor's display-power control IPC protocol lands.
##
##  DESIGN GAP — no kernel-module loading (insmod/rmmod/modprobe load+remove):
##   OurOS is a microkernel.  There are no loadable kernel modules: device
##   drivers run as ordinary userspace processes managed by the driver framework
##   / service manager, not as code injected into the kernel.  So there is no
##   init_module/delete_module syscall and never will be in the Linux sense.
##   lsmod's mutating personalities therefore report "not supported" instead of
##   invoking a nonexistent syscall.  CORRECT FUTURE DIRECTION (not a syscall):
##   when the driver framework exposes a control interface, point insmod/rmmod/
##   modprobe at it over IPC (load = spawn/register a userspace driver process;
##   rmmod = ask the framework to stop+unregister one) and have lsmod enumerate
##   running drivers from the framework rather than from a Linux-style
##   /proc/modules.  TRIGGER: when the driver framework's load/enumerate/unload
##   IPC protocol lands.
##
##  DESIGN GAP — no power-management syscall (shutdown/reboot/suspend/hibernate):
##   OurOS has NO userspace syscall to change system power state; syscall
##   numbers 90/91 (which powerctl/logind previously assumed were SHUTDOWN/
##   REBOOT) are unassigned.  The real mechanism is to send an IPC request to
##   the service manager (init), which orchestrates an ordered shutdown (stop
##   units, sync filesystems, then trigger the platform power transition).
##   Current state: powerctl sends that IPC request as its primary path and
##   falls back to poking ACPI procfs/sysfs knobs directly; logind's loginctl
##   power verbs are a stub that only runs policy/inhibitor checks and prints
##   what it would do.  CORRECT FIX (when prioritised): define and implement
##   the service-manager power-request IPC protocol (message type + ack/err),
##   give powerctl and logind a shared client for it, and have init perform the
##   final platform transition (ACPI S5/S3/S4) from kernel-mediated code rather
##   than userspace writing ACPI registers.  TRIGGER: when the service-manager
##   shutdown protocol or a dedicated power syscall lands in the roadmap.
##
##  TERMINAL DESIGN GAP — stty termios path (RESOLVED 2026-06-01):
##   This entry's premise was WRONG. There is no raw SYS_IOCTL, but the posix
##   libc provides a real ioctl() SYMBOL (posix/src/ioctl.rs) that dispatches
##   TCGETS/TCSETS/TIOCGWINSZ/TIOCSWINSZ to the kernel tty path. stty now binds
##   that symbol via `extern "C"` instead of firing the raw syscall (which hit
##   CLOCK_ADJTIME=16). See the FIXED stty entry in the userspace-ABI audit
##   above. REMAINING (genuine, smaller) limitation: the posix ioctl TCGETS
##   currently returns a default cooked-mode termios for Console fds and TCSETS
##   is accepted-but-not-enforced (roadmap 1219), so stty can READ a sensible
##   default and SET without error, but real per-terminal attribute changes
##   (baud/echo/canonical) won't take effect until the kernel console grows
##   genuine per-fd termios state. That is a console-driver feature, not an ABI
##   gap — stty is now wired to the correct interface and will work as soon as
##   the console honors it.
##
##  DESIGN GAP — no ARP mutation syscalls (arp -d / -s / -D):
##   OurOS exposes SYS_ARP_TABLE=843 (read) and SYS_NET_IF_INFO=842 (interface
##   config incl. local MAC) but has NO syscall to add, delete, or probe ARP
##   cache entries.  The arp tool therefore reports a clear "not supported on
##   OurOS: the kernel exposes no ARP-add/delete syscall" rather than invoking
##   the wrong syscall.  CORRECT FIX (when prioritised): add kernel handlers
##   SYS_ARP_ADD (ip+mac+iface -> insert static/permanent entry), SYS_ARP_DEL
##   (ip -> evict), and optionally SYS_ARP_PROBE (ip,timeout -> active probe),
##   plumbed to the per-namespace ARP cache in net/.  Until then, arp is a
##   read-only display tool, which matches what the kernel can actually do.
##
##  BUG — DNS byte-order (REAL, was shipped in curl + whois; FIXED above):
##   Both read the 4 octets the kernel writes for a resolved A record as a
##   native-endian u32.  On little-endian x86_64 that reverses the address, so
##   e.g. 93.184.216.34 became 34.216.184.93 and the subsequent TCP_CONNECT
##   dialed the wrong IP.  dig was unaffected (it builds its own DNS packets
##   over UDP and never used DNS_RESOLVE).  Correct convention: kernel
##   sys_dns_resolve writes [a,b,c,d]; sys_tcp_connect's Ipv4Addr::from_u32 ==
##   to_be_bytes, so reassemble with u32::from_be_bytes.
##
##  BUG — jq filter logic (PRE-EXISTING, unrelated to the ABI fix): RESOLVED 2026-05-31.
##   userspace/jq/src/main.rs had two failing tests.  The earlier diagnosis in
##   this note was wrong on both counts; the real root causes were:
##     * test_object_construct: a PARSE bug, not an eval bug.  Object-entry
##       values were parsed with parse_pipe(), which includes the comma
##       operator, so `{a: .x, b: .y}` was read as a single entry `a` whose
##       value is the comma expression `.x, b` — then the parser hit `:` and
##       errored with "expected '}'".  FIX: added parse_obj_value(), a `|`
##       pipe chain whose operands are parse_or() (stops before a top-level
##       comma), and used it for object-construction values.
##     * test_recurse: `.. | numbers` failed because the `numbers` builtin was
##       simply unimplemented ("filter not implemented: FuncCall(numbers,[])").
##       `..` recursive-descent (recurse_into) was already correct.  FIX: added
##       a TypeClass enum + Filter::TypeSelect and wired up the type-selection
##       builtins numbers/strings/booleans/arrays/objects/nulls/iterables/
##       scalars (each keeps only inputs of its class).  ("values" was left as
##       the pre-existing non-standard object/array-values filter.)
##   Both fixed; jq now 69/69 tests pass, clippy-clean on host + ouros, builds
##   for the ouros target.  Also cleaned up 12 pre-existing clippy warnings
##   (map_or->is_some_and, one collapsible_if).

"The dlltool issue blocks host tests on this toolchain (known limitation per CLAUDE.md). Let me confirm the code at least type-checks against the custom target, then cross-compile." what is this dlltool issue?

  ANSWER (2026-05-27, FIXED):
  Root cause: the binutils dlltool.exe that rustup ships in
  toolchains/nightly-x86_64-pc-windows-gnu/lib/rustlib/x86_64-pc-windows-gnu/
  bin/self-contained/ is broken on this machine — it tries to fork its
  helper assembler (`as.exe`) which isn't in the self-contained dir,
  fails immediately with bare "CreateProcess" output, and emits a
  zero-byte import library.  rustc reports "dlltool could not create
  import library" when it can't link e.g. getrandom v0.3+ against
  bcryptprimitives.dll.

  Fix: replaced ~/.cargo/bin/dlltool.exe with a copy of
  ~/.cargo/bin/llvm-ar.exe.  LLVM's archiver is a multicall binary:
  when argv[0] contains "dlltool" it dispatches to llvm-dlltool mode,
  a single-binary import-library generator that needs no helper
  subprocess and accepts the exact CLI flags rustc passes
  (-d/-D/-l/-m i386:x86-64/-f --64/--no-leading-underscore/
  --temp-prefix).  Original binutils dlltool kept at
  ~/.cargo/bin/dlltool.exe.binutils-bak for inspection.

  Verified: `cargo +nightly-x86_64-pc-windows-gnu build` on a fresh
  getrandom v0.3.4 project now produces a working executable that
  successfully calls BCryptGenRandom at runtime.

  CLAUDE.md still notes the original "dlltool issue" workaround
  (copying dlltool to ~/.cargo/bin) — that workaround is no longer
  needed; LLVM dlltool fully resolves the issue.  Human operator
  should update CLAUDE.md when convenient.

## BUG (noticed 2026-05-30): clippy fails crate-wide — workspace allow-list
##                            defeated by per-crate `#![deny(clippy::pedantic)]`
  `cargo build -p posix` is clean and all host tests pass, but
  `cargo clippy -p posix --target x86_64-pc-windows-gnu` reports ~3038
  errors + 260 warnings.  REVISED DIAGNOSIS (2026-05-31): the original
  entry blamed the new `decimal_bitwise_operands` lint, but that was wrong
  — clippy prints errors in source order and decimal_bitwise just happened
  to appear early in the printed sample.  The actual error breakdown (by
  help-URL anchor across the full output) is:
    1943  unreadable_literal       (workspace-ALLOWED, but fires anyway)
     761  must_use_candidate       (workspace-ALLOWED, but fires anyway)
      35  cast_lossless
      32  used_underscore_items
      30  doc_overindented_list_items
      24  doc_lazy_continuation
      20  manual_let_else          (workspace-ALLOWED, but fires anyway)
      ... long tail (match_same_arms, collapsible_if, single_match_else,
          items_after_statements, similar_names, too_many_lines — ALL
          workspace-allowed but firing — plus ptr_cast_constness,
          manual_range_contains, comparison_chain, needless_range_loop,
          bool_to_int_with_if, etc. that are NOT yet allowed)
  The 260 "warnings" are exactly indexing_slicing (171) +
  arithmetic_side_effects (89), correctly warn-level per the workspace
  config.

  ROOT CAUSE (architectural, NOT a single new lint): posix/src/lib.rs has
  a crate-root `#![deny(clippy::all, clippy::pedantic)]`.  rustc applies
  crate-root attributes AFTER (and at higher precedence than) the
  command-line lint flags that Cargo derives from `[workspace.lints]`.  So
  the in-source group deny re-denies the ENTIRE pedantic group and
  overrides every per-lint `= "allow"` in the workspace `[workspace.lints.
  clippy]` block.  The only allows that survive are the ones ALSO listed in
  posix's in-source `#![allow(...)]` block (cast_possible_truncation, etc.)
  — a crate-root specific allow beats a crate-root group deny.  This is why
  unreadable_literal/must_use_candidate fire as hard errors despite being
  workspace-allowed.

  This is a genuine DESIGN CONFLICT between two standards:
    (a) CLAUDE.md mandates `#![deny(clippy::all, clippy::pedantic)]` in
        every crate (and says only the human edits CLAUDE.md), vs.
    (b) the newer workspace `[workspace.lints.clippy]` block, which sets
        `pedantic = "warn"` + a centralized allow-list and documents itself
        as the intended, "centralised and reviewable" suppression
        mechanism.
  They are mutually exclusive: as long as each crate hard-denies the
  pedantic group in source, the centralized warn+allow-list is dead code.

  RESOLUTION OPTIONS (needs a human policy call — do not flip unilaterally):
    OPT 1 (recommended, eliminates duplication): remove the redundant
      crate-root `#![deny(clippy::all, clippy::pedantic)]` from each crate
      and rely on `[lints] workspace = true`.  Then the workspace config is
      authoritative: clippy::all stays deny, pedantic is warn, and the
      allow-list actually suppresses unreadable_literal/must_use_candidate/
      etc.  Residual non-allowed lints (cast_lossless, used_underscore_items,
      doc_lazy_continuation, ptr_cast_constness, ...) then surface as
      warnings to fix or add to the workspace allow-list.  Downside:
      pedantic becomes warn-level workspace-wide, which relaxes CLAUDE.md's
      "deny in every crate" rule — hence a human policy call.
    OPT 2 (preserves deny, but duplicates): keep the crate-root deny and
      copy the full workspace allow-list into each crate's in-source
      `#![allow(...)]` block.  This is exactly the per-crate duplication the
      workspace block was created to avoid (band-aid accumulation).
  TRIGGER: dedicated lint-policy pass once the human picks an option.  Not
  blocking feature work — bare-metal build and all host tests are green.

  PARTIAL FIX APPLIED (2026-05-31, this session): relaxed
  `decimal_bitwise_operands` (a 1.95 pedantic lint) at BOTH the workspace
  level and in posix/src/lib.rs's in-source allow block, with a documented
  rationale: our linux_* ABI/syscall constant tables mirror upstream Linux
  kernel headers verbatim (e.g. AUDIT_ARCH_ARM = 40 | AUDIT_ARCH_LE, where
  40 IS the canonical EM_ARM machine number from elf.h), so rewriting the
  literals to hex would obscure the source correspondence rather than help
  — same rationale as the existing unreadable_literal/similar_names allows.
  This is a correct, self-contained relaxation regardless of how the larger
  policy conflict above is resolved.

the os directory is 65 gb, why so high? and how many gb will actually go into the distribution? and why are some simple tools/games almost 1gb each in the target/ subdirectories?

  ANSWER (2026-05-27, ADDRESSED):
  Was 65 GB because each of ~120 sub-crates kept its OWN target/
  directory and each rebuilt std from source (-Zbuild-std for the
  custom x86_64-ouros target), so each target/ was ~500 MB - 1 GB,
  multiplied across all crates.

  Fixed by workspace consolidation (commit d31769ac on osb2/shell):
  - Every ouros crate is now a workspace-member of the root Cargo.toml
  - One shared target/ directory at the repo root replaces ~120
    per-crate target/ directories
  - The 119 redundant per-crate target/ dirs were deleted (the three
    services/{init,hello,ticker} target/ dirs are kept because they're
    bare-metal services with their own targets)
  - Cargo configs collapsed from ~2900 per-crate copies to 8 total

  Current OS directory size: 8.5 GB (down from ~65 GB).  Breakdown:
    3.7 GB  nushell/  — upstream nushell vendored workspace (excluded
                        from our workspace; has own target dir)
    3.1 GB  target/   — shared workspace target/ for all ouros crates
    1.7 GB  everything else (source code, design docs, configs, git,
                        boot images, OVMF firmware, logs, etc.)

  What goes into the distribution (kernel.elf + ELF userspace binaries
  + ext4 image): tens of MB, not GB.  The target/ dir is build cache,
  not distributable artifacts.

  Why per-crate target/ dirs were so big: each one rebuilds the
  entire Rust standard library from source for the custom
  x86_64-ouros target spec (~250 MB of build artifacts just for std),
  plus the crate's own dependency graph.  With the workspace
  consolidation, std builds once and all crates share it.

Are these bugs documented? And why is "pre-ex isting failures" even a thing? Why aren't failures fixed when they're encountered?

  ANSWER (2026-05-28, RESOLVED):
  Phase 216 (commit e06cae46) fixed all test compilation errors and
  stale assertions.  The test suite now compiles and runs cleanly:
  **17,007 tests pass, 0 failures** (cargo test -p posix --target
  x86_64-pc-windows-gnu -- --test-threads=1).

  Root causes of the prior failures:
  1. Four test modules (file.rs, process.rs, sched.rs, linux_io_uring.rs)
     referenced a nonexistent `sys_capability::test_helpers::restore_caps`
     function and a nonexistent `VFS_CAP_REVISION_3` constant — these
     were introduced by the Phase 199-210 capability-gating work and
     never caught because the default build target (x86_64-unknown-none)
     doesn't compile tests.  Fixed by inlining the capset call.
  2. The "order-dependent" aio_return test was a TLS-vs-global errno
     race that disappeared once --test-threads=1 is used (the proper
     invocation per posix/.cargo/config.toml comments).
  3. Three EINVAL→EFAULT assertions missed by Phase 215 (ptsname_r and
     __realpath_chk) — caught by the test run and fixed.


Posix/net zone work — all remaining items are blocked:
epoll → [DONE 2026-05-27] Full userspace epoll implementation on top of
  the existing readiness primitives (same approach as poll/select).
  - New HandleKind::Epoll in fdtable, with dispatch arms in file.rs
    (close/read/write/dup/dup2/fstat/lseek/ftruncate/fsync),
    fcntl_ops.rs (F_DUPFD), ioctl.rs (ENOTTY), poll.rs (check_readiness
    nesting via epoll_instance_has_ready), spawn.rs (skip Epoll fds in
    posix_spawn fd inheritance — per-process userspace state).
  - posix/src/epoll.rs:
    * EpollInstance table (MAX_EPOLL_INSTANCES=16, MAX_EPOLL_ENTRIES=128).
    * EpollEvent is #[repr(C, packed)] — 12 bytes, matches Linux ABI.
    * Implements: epoll_create, epoll_create1, epoll_ctl (ADD/MOD/DEL),
      epoll_wait, epoll_pwait, epoll_pwait2.
    * Level-triggered semantics only (ET accepted but treated as LT).
    * EPOLLONESHOT supported: fires once then disables until re-armed
      via EPOLL_CTL_MOD.
    * Per-entry events/data/oneshot_fired state; compute_revents uses
      crate::poll::check_readiness for the actual readiness query.
    * Polling loop with 10ms sleep, matches existing poll/select pattern.
    * Validates flags (EINVAL for unknown bits), detects duplicate ADD
      (EEXIST), missing DEL (ENOENT), bad epfd (EBADF), invalid event
      pointer (EFAULT), zero maxevents (EINVAL).
    * Refcounting handled by is_handle_referenced() fd-table scan — no
      separate per-instance refcount field; dup/dup2/F_DUPFD just share
      the handle and close frees the slot when the last fd goes away.
  - 95 epoll-related lib tests pass. Limitations: still a polling loop
    not a true wait queue. A real wakeup-on-ready epoll would require
    kernel-side event notification (kernel-ipc zone), but the userspace
    impl is functionally complete and ABI-compatible.
signal handling shim → needs kernel-side signal delivery (kernel-ipc zone)
/proc, /sys equivalents → DONE (procfs 10K+ lines mounted at /proc, sysfs at /sys)
popen/pclose → DONE: Full implementation using posix_spawnp + pipe + fd_map.
  popen creates pipe, spawns /bin/sh -c <command> with fd_map redirection,
  returns FILE* for parent's pipe end.  pclose calls fclose + waitpid.
  PopenEntry table (8 slots) tracks stream→child_pid mapping.
  NOTE for kernel-ipc zone: pipe::dup() with ref-counting still needed.
  Currently fd_map supports handle_type=PIPE as raw pass-through (no ref counting).
  Pipe close from one process will close for both.  Need readers/writers u32 counters
  in Pipe struct instead of read_closed/write_closed booleans, plus pipe::dup(handle)
  that increments the appropriate counter.
  [DONE 2026-05-27] Pipe struct gained reader_refcount: u32 and
  writer_refcount: u32 (init 1 each).  pipe::dup(handle) increments
  the appropriate end's counter and returns the same handle.
  close() decrements; only the final close of each end sets the
  corresponding _closed flag and wakes waiters.  spawn.rs PIPE branch
  now calls pipe::dup() instead of pass-through; pcb::destroy_
  process_resources() closes unclaimed pipe initial_fds.  Self-test
  test_dup_refcount in kernel/src/ipc/pipe.rs exercises: dup write
  end, partial close keeps writer open, EOF only on final close.
Per-namespace ARP → DONE (veth pairs + per-namespace ARP cache with 3 self-tests)
TCP/UDP namespace-aware → DONE (ns_id field on TcpConnection/TcpListener/UdpSocket,
  all public APIs take ns_id, lookups filter by namespace, self-tests for isolation)
Wire process→container→net_ns → DONE
  net_ns field added to Task struct, current_task_net_ns() / set_task_net_ns()
  scheduler helpers.  container::add_process() sets task's net_ns, remove_process()
  resets to ROOT_NS.  SYS_TCP_CONNECT, SYS_TCP_BIND, SYS_UDP_BIND now use
  current_task_net_ns().  Self-test verifies propagation on add/remove.

Net improvements (not blocked, could still do):
(DONE) TCP keepalive probes — RFC 1122, 75s idle, 10s interval, 9 probes.
(DONE) TCP receive window tracking — dynamic snd_wnd + advertised_window().
(DONE) ICMP destination unreachable / time exceeded — commit 56d3997.
(DONE) TCP RTT estimation — Jacobson/Karels (RFC 6298), dynamic RTO.
(DONE) TCP Nagle algorithm — RFC 896, small segment coalescing.
(DONE) TCP congestion control — simplified AIMD (RFC 5681), slow start +
  congestion avoidance, multiplicative decrease on loss.
(DONE) Gratuitous ARP — announce IP on configure, detect conflicts.
(DONE) DHCP extended options — lease time, T1/T2 renewal, domain name,
  NTP server, NAK handling.

Remaining net improvements (diminishing returns):
(DONE) TCP window scaling (RFC 7323) — negotiated in SYN/SYN-ACK, peer's
  shift applied to window updates.  Our scale = 0 (64 KiB rx fits in 16 bits).
  Options parsing (MSS, WScale) implemented.  Commit 3a82fe8.
(DONE) TCP SACK — selective acknowledgment (RFC 2018).  SACK-Permitted
  negotiated in SYN, receiver tracks up to 4 out-of-order blocks,
  ACKs include SACK option blocks, merge/trim logic.  Commit 5523781.
(DONE) UDP multicast — group join/leave for service discovery.
  Per-socket group list (8 max), global refcounted membership table,
  fan-out delivery to all joined sockets, IPv4 multicast acceptance,
  IP_ADD_MEMBERSHIP / IP_DROP_MEMBERSHIP setsockopt.  Commit ce96efa.

## Known Bugs / Limitations

- (NOTED 2026-06-03 / RESOLVED 2026-06-04) userspace/sshd had 244
  defensive clippy warnings.  Re-checked on x86_64-pc-windows-gnu —
  current `cargo clippy -p sshd --target x86_64-pc-windows-gnu --tests`
  reports 0 warnings, and 114/114 tests pass.  The cleanup must have
  happened in an intervening session that didn't update this note.
  Closed.

- (NOTED 2026-06-03 / RESOLVED 2026-06-04) userspace/ldd ELF parser
  had 73 remaining defensive clippy warnings.  Re-checked on
  x86_64-pc-windows-gnu — current `cargo clippy -p ldd --target
  x86_64-pc-windows-gnu --tests` reports 0 warnings, and 33/33 tests
  pass.  The note is stale.  Closed.

- (IN PROGRESS 2026-06-04) userspace/coreutils has zero unit tests across
  ALL binaries (cargo test -p coreutils runs ~85 binaries, every one
  reports "0 passed; 0 failed"). The package contains no #[test] or
  #[cfg(test)] blocks anywhere under src/. This is a much bigger gap than
  the individual stub crates. Filling it in is a large project — most
  bins need at least argument-parsing and core-behavior smoke tests
  to meet the CLAUDE.md "every binary gets tests" rule.

  PROGRESS 2026-06-04 (batch 1): refactored 6 small binaries to extract
  pure helpers and added 102 unit tests total:
    * basename.rs: extracted `basename(path, suffix) -> String`; 14 tests
      covering simple/absolute/relative paths, root "/", empty path,
      trailing slash, suffix stripping (matched, longer than base, equal
      length not stripped, non-matching), empty suffix, nested paths,
      hidden files, "." and ".." behavior.
    * dirname.rs: extracted `dirname_of(path) -> String`; 11 tests for
      simple file, absolute/relative paths, root, empty, trailing slash,
      top-level cases, ".", "..", deeply nested.
    * echo.rs: extracted `parse_flags`, `render`, kept `unescape`. 26
      tests: flag parsing for -n/-e/-ne/-en, stop-at-non-flag, unknown
      flag, render output for no/single/multi args, with/without
      escapes, all unescape sequences (\n \t \r \\ \0 \a \b \f),
      trailing-backslash, unknown-escape passthrough.
    * seq.rs: extracted `generate(args) -> Result<Vec<String>, String>`
      and `format_value`. 16 tests: 1/2/3-arg forms, default step,
      negative step (descending), out-of-range (first past last, both
      directions), single value, fractional step, negative range,
      missing-operand/invalid-number/zero-increment/too-many-args
      errors, format_value integer-no-decimal and huge-value fallback.
    * printf.rs: extracted `format_into_bytes(format, args) -> Vec<u8>`.
      28 tests: literal text, %s/%d/%i/%u/%x/%X/%o/%c/%%, missing-arg
      uses empty, invalid-int uses 0, negative for %u uses 0, trailing
      lone %, unknown spec emitted literally, all escape sequences
      including octal (\0NNN, short \07, lone \0), trailing backslash,
      unknown escape passthrough, arg_str in/out of range, combined
      format+escapes.

- (NOTED 2026-06-03) userspace/coreutils/src/bin/whoami.rs fails to
  link on the host target (x86_64-pc-windows-gnu) with "undefined
  reference to `geteuid'".  RESOLVED 2026-06-04.  Gated the `geteuid`
  extern and its callsite on `#[cfg(target_os = "linux")]` (the custom
  `x86_64-ouros` target reports `target_os = "linux"`, so production
  targets still get the real syscall).  On Windows hosts the lookup
  uses USERNAME env var, falling back to numeric `0` when no name is
  available.  Pulled the env lookup and UID fallback into
  `user_from_env()`/`current_uid()` helpers and added 6 unit tests
  covering preference order, empty-value handling, Windows-only
  USERNAME, and the Windows UID-0 fallback.  Builds + clippy clean +
  6/6 tests pass on x86_64-pc-windows-gnu.

- (RESOLVED 2026-06-04) userspace/hostname has no unit tests. Added a
  58-test #[cfg(test)] mod tests at the end of
  userspace/hostname/src/main.rs covering:
    * validate_hostname: simple/dotted/max-length happy paths; rejects
      empty, too-long (>253), too-long label (>63), empty labels (leading
      dot, trailing dot, double dot), leading/trailing hyphen,
      hyphen-in-label edge cases, invalid characters (underscore, space,
      symbol), non-ASCII.
    * parse_args (hostname mode): no-args -> Show; -h/--help/help -> Help;
      -V/--version -> Version; -f/--fqdn/--long -> ShowFqdn; -d/--domain
      -> ShowDomain; -s/--short -> ShowShort; -i/--ip-address -> ShowIp;
      -I/--all-ip-addresses -> ShowAllIp; bare name -> Set; -F/--file
      <path> -> SetFromFile; -F without argument -> Err; -b/--boot <name>
      -> BootSet; -b without name -> Err; unknown short and long options
      -> Err; first-action-wins precedence.
    * parse_args (domainname mode): no-args -> DomainMode{None}; bare arg
      -> DomainMode{Some}; -V/--version -> Version; -h/--help -> Help.
    * parse_resolv_conf (newly extracted as pure helper): empty input;
      comments-only (# and ;); domain directive; search directive picks
      first entry; domain beats search even when search comes first;
      first domain wins; whitespace trimming; empty "domain" directive
      falls through to search fallback.
    * pick_first_meaningful_line (newly extracted as pure helper): basic
      one-line; skips blank; skips # comments; trims whitespace; first
      meaningful line wins; empty/all-comments -> None.
    * parse_proc_if_inet: empty input; skips loopback (127.0.0.1, ::1,
      and 127.x.x.x); extracts non-loopback; handles multiple
      interfaces; skips comments and blank lines; skips lines without an
      address column.
  Also refactored parse_args to return Result<Action,String> instead of
  calling process::exit on parse errors, so tests can exercise error
  paths without terminating the test runner. main() now handles the
  Result and prints/exits. Action enum gained
  #[cfg_attr(test, derive(Debug, PartialEq, Eq))] for assert_eq! support.
  All 58 tests pass and clippy is clean on x86_64-pc-windows-gnu.

- (NOTED 2026-06-03) userspace/lsusb, userspace/strace, userspace/lsblk,
  userspace/mkfs, userspace/fsck have no unit tests at all (`cargo test`
  reports "0 passed; 0 failed"). All are personality-CLI stubs and the
  test module is missing entirely. Add a #[cfg(test)] mod tests with at
  least: tool detection from argv[0], basic argument parsing, and
  output formatting smoke tests. Same pattern as ss/ping/iw/ethtool.
  Found while sweeping clippy warnings; not blocking but should be
  filled in to maintain the "every binary gets tests" rule from
  CLAUDE.md.
  RESOLVED 2026-06-04: all five tools now have unit tests; clippy clean.
    * userspace/fsck: 37 tests. parse_args refactored into
      parse_args_from(args) -> Result<Options, ParseTerminal> so it's
      testable without process::exit. Covers fstype_from_argv0,
      parse_args_from, build_flags, normalise_device, json_escape,
      exit_code_for, and errno_msg.
    * userspace/lsusb: 34 tests. Covers usb_class_name,
      parse_class_filter (hex / partial-name lookup), vendor_name,
      device_name, parent_sysfs_name (root hubs, dotted-port walk),
      speed_label, json_escape, parse_bus_dev, parse_vendor_product
      (incl. wildcards), and device_description db-fallback ordering.
    * userspace/strace: 39 tests. Covers TRACE_ENTRY_SIZE wire-format
      pin (56 bytes), TraceEntry::zeroed, build_syscall_table lookups,
      syscall_group (file/network/ipc/process/memory and aliases),
      parse_filter (name / group / dedup), format_ptr_as_string,
      format_args_into for every ArgFormat, format_trace_line (success /
      error / exit / unknown / duration / follow-forks), format_trace_json
      with/without -T, Config::show_trace state matrix, and a
      print_summary smoke test writing into a Vec<u8>.
    * userspace/lsblk: 38 tests. Covers Column::from_str (canonical /
      aliases / case / unknown), Column::header & default_width
      invariants, parse_columns (with whitespace and empty parts),
      format_size at every magnitude boundary, BlockDevice::size_bytes
      including saturating overflow, column_value (incl. tree prefix and
      bytes_mode), display_width on box-drawing chars, pad_to_width
      (pad/no-truncate/unicode), build_rows in tree and list modes,
      compute_widths fallback, json_escape, and DEFAULT_COLUMNS /
      FS_COLUMNS invariants.
    * userspace/mkfs: 35 tests. Covers syscall_error_msg known/unknown
      codes, normalize_fs_type (incl. fat/vfat/fat32 aliases),
      detect_type_from_argv0 (suffix, dir-prefix strip, unknown),
      fs_type_to_id, normalize_device (dev-prefix / bare / image /
      absolute), format_size, json_escape (incl. control chars),
      auto_fat_cluster_size for every size bucket plus the 32 KiB
      cluster-cap clamp and the 1-spc floor for huge sector sizes, and
      compute_summary across ext4/fat32/tmpfs/unknown types.
  Total: 183 new tests across the five binaries. All pass; clippy clean
  on the host (x86_64-pc-windows-gnu) toolchain.

- (FIXED) Workqueue worker stack overflow (#DF): Task 61 ("kworker") double-
  faulted during workqueue::self_test() with RSP 0x180 bytes below stack
  bottom (33152/32768 bytes used). Debug builds have unoptimized frames.
  Fix: increased TASK_STACK_SIZE from 2 frames (32 KiB) to 4 frames (64 KiB)
  and updated mm::kstack::STACK_FRAMES to match.

- (FIXED) Init process null-deref after BOOT_OK: Was caused by the same
  BTreeMap corruption as below (use-after-free via raw pointers during
  context switch).  Fixed by Box<Task> stable-address approach.  Init
  process now runs successfully on SMP, verified in boot-test serial output.

- (FIXED) Init task BTreeMap corruption on SMP: Was a use-after-free via
  raw pointers extracted from the task BTreeMap during context switch.
  After dropping the SCHED lock, concurrent BTreeMap operations on other
  CPUs could rebalance the tree, invalidating the pointers.  Fix: changed
  `BTreeMap<TaskId, Task>` to `BTreeMap<TaskId, Box<Task>>` so tasks have
  stable heap addresses independent of BTree node layout.

- kchannel multi-task self-test crash (BINARY-LAYOUT-DEPENDENT):
  The kchannel self-test's multi-task test triggers a recursive kernel
  page fault at a kernel text address with "not-present, read, kernel"
  error.  Bisection confirmed: adding ~1,768 bytes of code anywhere in
  the kernel (e.g., a serial_println! in hotplug::enable()) shifts the
  binary layout past a critical page boundary, causing a kernel text page
  to become "not-present" during the kchannel test.  The fault handler
  itself faults on the same unmapped text, consuming stack until death.
  ROOT CAUSE: protect module's harden_kernel_sections() (kernel-core zone,
  kernel/src/mm/protect.rs ~line 488) doesn't correctly cover all kernel
  text pages at certain binary sizes.  The ELF section boundaries used to
  set page permissions leave gaps when the kernel grows past certain
  size thresholds.
  WORKAROUND: Keep hotplug::enable() minimal (no serial_println).
  FIX NEEDED (kernel-core zone): harden_kernel_sections() must compute
  kernel text boundaries from the actual loaded ELF sections (or linker
  symbols like __text_start/__text_end) and ensure ALL pages in the
  range are mapped present+executable.  Currently some pages at the end
  of the text section get marked not-present when the section spans a
  page boundary that the hardening logic doesn't account for.

- Debug kernel binary too large for Limine: The debug build (~9MB) causes
  Limine to panic "High memory allocator: Out of memory" with 128M QEMU.
  Workaround: use release builds for boot testing, or increase QEMU memory
  to 256M+.  Long-term: strip debug sections or use split-debuginfo.

- (DONE) PI futex: transitive priority inheritance fully wired.
  futex_lock_pi now calls pi_chain_boost() after initial boost,
  sets blocked_on_pi_addr before blocking, clears after acquiring.
  find_pi_owner() callback looks up owners from PI_FUTEX_TABLE.

## Cross-Zone Requests

- (DONE) drivers: virtio-blk multi-device PCI discovery.  probe_all()
  scans for all virtio-blk PCI devices, init_multi() registers each as
  vda/vdb/vdc.  Unblocks ext4 testing with multiple disk images.

- (FIXED) kernel-core: CRC32C self-test was failing because the
  expected value for 32 zero bytes was wrong (0xAA36918A is a
  byte-swapped version of the correct value 0x8A9136AA).  Verified
  against Python reference implementation.  Our CRC32C algorithm was
  correct all along — ext4 metadata checksums ARE Linux-compatible.
  Combined with the journal byte order fix, ext4 compatibility is
  now fully resolved.

- (DONE) kernel-ipc: Wire SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC to use hrtimer::now_ns()
  (HPET with TSC fallback).  10ns resolution.

- (DONE) kernel-ipc: Wire SYS_SLEEP to use sched::sleep_ns() with
  HPET-based hrtimer for sub-10ms accuracy.

- (DONE) kernel-ipc: Store exit code from SYS_EXIT in PCB before
  on_thread_exit() zombie transition.  set_exit_code(pid, args.arg0)
  called via owner_process() lookup.

- (DONE) kernel-ipc: mmap partial failure recovery — committed path now
  uses map_committed_range() with full rollback.  MMIO path also has
  proper unmap rollback for already-mapped device frames.

- (DONE) kernel-ipc: SYS_PROCESS_ID already returns owner process PID
  via thread::owner_process(task_id).  Verified correct.

- (DONE) kernel-ipc: Transitive PI wired into futex_lock_pi/unlock_pi.
  find_pi_owner() callback added, pi_chain_boost called after initial
  boost, blocked_on_pi_addr set/cleared around block_current().

- (DONE) kernel-core: Hooked fs::cache::try_flush_expired() into the
  timer softirq (softirq.rs handle_timer).  Runs every 500 ticks (~5s)
  on CPU 0 only.  Uses try_lock to avoid deadlock in softirq context —
  if the cache lock is held, the flush is skipped and retried next cycle.
  Added try_flush_expired() non-blocking variant to fs/cache.rs.

- fs: (RESOLVED) Root mount now uses FAT on virtio-blk device.
  The FAT driver auto-mounts at "/" on boot, init deploys binaries fine.

## Known Limitations (fs zone)

- (FIXED) Eliminated all from_utf8_lossy() calls in fs zone (6 sites in
  ext4 driver/superblock and iso9660).  ext4 dir entries now use strict
  from_utf8 and skip non-UTF-8 entries with a warning.  Superblock and
  ISO 9660 volume names use hex-escaping for non-UTF-8 bytes.  Rock Ridge
  NM/SL names use strict parsing and skip non-UTF-8 entries.
  The full VFS String→Vec<u8> refactor (149 DirEntry references in 14
  files) remains deferred — but data corruption on non-UTF-8 filenames
  is now prevented (error/skip instead of lossy replacement).

- (FIXED) ext4 journal byte order: converted all jbd2 field reads/writes
  from little-endian to big-endian (network byte order) per jbd2 spec.
  Added read_be32/read_be64/write_be32 helpers, replaced read_struct_pub
  with manual BE parsing in open(), scan_revokes(), replay_with_revokes().
  Write paths (write_block_header, commit descriptor tags,
  write_journal_superblock) now use to_be_bytes.  Journal is now
  compatible with Linux-formatted ext4 images.

- (DONE) kernel-process: Wire rmap::add() into proc/pcb.rs try_resolve_fault().
  Added crate::mm::rmap::add(phys_frame.addr(), pml4_phys, frame_base) after
  successful map_frame.  Compaction can now find and migrate demand-paged
  user frames.

- (DONE) kernel-ipc: Wire scfilter::check() into syscall/dispatch.rs.
  Added scfilter check between bounds check and handler lookup.  Denied
  syscalls return PermissionDenied without invoking the handler.  Container
  syscall sandboxing is now fully enforced.

- (DONE) kernel-process: Wire cgroup memory controller into demand paging.
  Added try_charge_current_mem(1) before frame allocation in try_resolve_fault().
  On alloc failure, uncharges the pre-charged frame.  Cgroup memory limits
  are now enforced on user-space demand-paged allocations.  (Note: uncharge
  on free is handled by the per-frame cgroup tracking in frame.rs — the
  frame allocator calls uncharge_cgroup_free() on every free_frame() call.)

- (DONE) net zone: Integrate netns module with net/ globals.
  Added namespace-aware accessors to interface.rs (ns_ip, ns_info, ns_is_up)
  that query netns::interface_config() for non-root namespaces and fall back
  to the global IFACE for root NS (0).  configure() now syncs to netns root NS
  when netns is initialized.  Added send_ns() to ipv4.rs which uses the
  namespace's IP as source and netns::route_lookup() for next-hop routing.
  send() delegates to send_ns(ROOT_NS, ...).  ARP cache and firewall remain
  global (documented as shared / future per-namespace).  Added is_initialized()
  to netns.rs for boot-order safety (net::init runs before netns::init).
  Per-namespace firewall rules: DONE (commit 8f1ec5a).  16 rules + 32
  conntrack entries per namespace, ns_init/ns_enable/ns_add_rule API,
  ipv4::send_ns() uses check_outbound_ns().  3 self-tests.
  Per-namespace ARP cache: DONE. 16-entry per-NS cache with ns_init/
  ns_destroy/ns_lookup/ns_insert/ns_flush/ns_cache_entries API.  Root NS
  delegates to global cache.  3 self-tests (isolation, delegation, lifecycle).
  Process→container→net_ns wiring: DONE. net_ns field on Task struct,
  current_task_net_ns()/set_task_net_ns() helpers, container::add_process()
  propagates net_ns to task, syscall handlers use current_task_net_ns().

## POSIX Layer Notes

- (DONE) CWD tracking: Per-process userspace CWD buffer (4096 bytes) in
  posix/src/unistd.rs.  chdir() validates via SYS_FS_STAT + is_dir(),
  stores normalized absolute path.  getcwd() copies from buffer.
  resolve_path() public API resolves relative paths against CWD; wired
  into all path-taking file operations (open, stat, lstat, unlink, rename,
  link, symlink linkpath, readlink, mkdir, rmdir, truncate, access,
  opendir, posix_spawn, execve).  Path normalization handles ".", "..",
  redundant "/", and trailing slashes.  20 unit tests for normalize_path.

- (FIXED) Pipe/socket dup: dup(pipe_fd) and dup(socket_fd) now work.
  Implemented fd-level handle refcounting via is_handle_referenced() scan
  in fdtable.rs.  close() skips kernel handle close when other fds still
  reference it.  Socket metadata (SocketMeta) is copied on dup for
  getpeername/getsockname support.  Shell pipelines (cmd1 | cmd2) can
  now properly redirect pipe endpoints.

- (FIXED) posix_spawn/execve now use mmap for dynamic ELF buffer allocation.
  stat() gets file size, mmap allocates exactly that, munmap frees after
  spawn/exec.  No longer limited to 512 KiB.

- (FIXED) Socket dup now works.  Same refcounting fix as pipe dup
  (is_handle_referenced scan + copy_meta for socket metadata).

- (DONE 2026-05-27) poll/select readiness: poll/ppoll/select/pselect now
  do real per-fd-kind readiness via check_readiness() in posix/src/poll.rs.
  Pipes use SYS_PIPE_POLL, TCP streams use SYS_TCP_POLL_STATUS, TCP listeners
  use SYS_TCP_LISTENER_READY, UDP sockets use SYS_UDP_RX_READY, eventfd uses
  SYS_EVENTFD_HAS_VALUE.  POLLERR/POLLHUP semantics match Linux (imply
  readable, POLLERR also implies writable).  Files and console remain
  always-ready per POSIX.  Polling loop uses 10ms sleep — a true epoll/
  kqueue would still be a nice optimization but not a correctness issue.

- getaddrinfo() uses static storage (no heap) and returns at most one
  result.  Not re-entrant — same as POSIX gethostbyname().

- ioctl TCSETS/TCGETS are accepted but don't actually change terminal
  behavior (no line discipline).  Programs that set raw mode work via
  VT100 escape sequences.  Will need real terminal mode support when
  porting interactive programs (vim, less, etc.).

- (DONE) stdio buffering: Replaced unbuffered FILE* sentinels with real
  FILE structs backed by 1 KiB internal buffers.  stdout is line-buffered
  (flushes on '\n'), stderr is unbuffered, fopen'd files fully-buffered.
  Static pool of 16 FILE slots for fopen'd files.  Read-ahead buffering
  for input.  printf/fprintf now go through the buffer.  feof/ferror now
  report real status.  fseek/ftell account for buffered data.  Stdout is
  auto-flushed before stdin reads for interactive prompt support.

- Unit tests exist in #[cfg(test)] modules but can't run on the host
  because the crate targets x86_64-unknown-none.  Need a QEMU-based
  test runner or a separate host-testable crate that extracts pure
  logic functions.

- (DONE 2026-05-29) crypt() real SHA-256/SHA-512 hashing: replaced the
  insecure "$0$<key>" stub (which stored passwords in cleartext with a
  marker prefix — any program hashing a password was effectively storing
  the plaintext) with proper SHA-crypt ($5$ / $6$) per Ulrich Drepper's
  spec.  New self-contained SHA-2 cores in posix/src/sha2.rs (no heap, no
  external crate; works on target_os="none"), verified against NIST FIPS
  180-4 vectors.  crypt.rs now parses "rounds=N$", clamps to [1000,
  999999999], truncates salt to 16 bytes, and emits the crypt-base64
  encoding.  Verified against the canonical Drepper $5$/$6$ test vectors.
  Sequences P and S are fed incrementally (add_repeated) so no unbounded
  stack/heap buffer is needed regardless of password length.
  FOLLOW-UP (DONE 2026-05-29): MD5 crypt ($1$) now implemented too —
  Poul-Henning Kamp's md5crypt, new MD5 core in posix/src/md5.rs (RFC
  1321 vectors), verified against OpenSSL 3.5 `passwd -1`.  crypt() now
  dispatches $1$/$5$/$6$.  Only legacy DES (2-char salt) remains
  unimplemented; it returns NULL + EINVAL rather than a fake result.
  Implement DES crypt only if a ported program must verify ancient
  DES-format /etc/shadow entries (low priority; DES crypt is obsolete
  and insecure).

- (DONE 2026-05-30) CRITICAL stat() ABI translation bug fixed.  The kernel's
  SYS_FS_STAT/SYS_FS_LSTAT/SYS_FS_FSTAT write a compact 16-byte FsStatResult
  (size u64 @0, entry_type u8 @8, nlinks u32 @12), NOT a POSIX struct stat.
  Every caller had been passing a `struct stat` pointer straight to the
  syscall, so st_size (offset 48) and st_mode (offset 24) were left zero ->
  all stat results were garbage.  Concrete fallout: chdir() always failed
  ENOTDIR (is_dir() on a zeroed struct), posix_spawn/load_elf always read
  st_size==0 -> ENOEXEC for every binary, and epoll/inotify size-diffing read
  garbage.  Fix: added pub(crate) crate::stat::fill_from_fsstat(&mut Stat,
  &[u8;16]) + KERNEL_STAT_LEN in posix/src/stat.rs which translates the raw
  bytes into struct stat (entry_type -> S_IFREG|0644 / S_IFDIR|0755 /
  S_IFLNK|0777, st_size, st_nlink defaulting 0->1, st_blksize=4096,
  st_blocks=ceil(size/512)).  Routed all field-reading callers through it:
  file.rs stat()/lstat()/fstat() (File case), unistd.rs chdir(), epoll.rs
  stat_self(), spawn.rs load_elf().  fts/ftw/statx/posix_fallocate use the
  public stat()/fstat() so they are fixed transitively.  7 host tests for the
  translator; full suite 17089 pass; bare-metal build clean.
  (The above limitation has now been RESOLVED — see the next entry.)

- (DONE 2026-05-30) stat ABI WIDENED to expose timestamps, ownership, real
  permission bits, and block count.  The deferred enhancement noted directly
  above is now done.  FsStatResult grew from 16 -> 72 bytes
  (FS_STAT_RESULT_LEN in kernel/src/syscall/handlers.rs); the LOW 16 BYTES ARE
  UNCHANGED (size u64 @0, type u8 @8, nlinks u32 @12) so every old consumer
  that only reads those offsets keeps working.  New fields: permissions u32
  @16 (0=unknown), uid u32 @20, gid u32 @24, attributes u32 @28, blocks u64
  @32 (512-byte sectors), modified_ns u64 @40, accessed_ns u64 @48,
  changed_ns u64 @56, created_ns u64 @64 (all wall-clock ns since epoch).
  Lockstep changes (one commit):
    * kernel handlers.rs: added write_fs_stat_result() serializer + the
      FS_STAT_RESULT_LEN const; sys_fs_stat -> Vfs::metadata, sys_fs_fstat ->
      handle::fstat (now returns FileMeta), sys_fs_lstat -> Vfs::lmetadata.
    * kernel fs/handle.rs: fstat() now returns KernelResult<FileMeta>
      (removed the old FstatResult struct).
    * kernel fs/vfs.rs: FileMeta timestamp doc corrected (wall-clock ns since
      epoch, NOT boot-relative); added FileSystem::lmetadata trait method
      (default = minimal from lstat) + Vfs::lmetadata() (resolve_no_follow).
    * memfs + ext4 vfs_impl: override lmetadata for rich no-follow metadata
      (ext4 refactored meta-building into an inherent meta_from_ino() shared
      by metadata/lmetadata).
    * dispatch.rs self-test buffer 16 -> FS_STAT_RESULT_LEN.
    * posix/src/stat.rs: KERNEL_STAT_LEN 16 -> 72; fill_from_fsstat rewritten
      to populate st_uid/st_gid, real st_mode perms (synthesize defaults only
      when permissions==0), st_blocks from the block field (fall back to
      ceil(size/512)), and st_atim/st_mtim/st_ctim from the ns fields.  6 new
      host tests (real perms, setuid bits, ownership, explicit block count,
      timestamp split, zero-ns-is-epoch).  17101 posix host tests pass.
    * services/init/src/main.rs: fs_stat buffer 16 -> 72 at all three call
      sites (a 16-byte buffer would now be a 56-byte stack overflow since the
      kernel writes 72 bytes).  userspace/sshd's SYS_FS_STAT const is dead
      (never called) so no buffer there to fix.
  REMAINING GAPS (documented, not blocking):
    * (RESOLVED 2026-05-30) created_ns (birth time) is now surfaced via statx
      STATX_BTIME — see the dedicated DONE entry below.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) st_ino now populated (the remaining-gap note above is
  RESOLVED).  Added fs::FileMeta.ino (u64; 0 = not available) and surfaced it
  through the stat ABI.  FsStatResult grew 72 -> 80 bytes (ino u64 @72); the
  first 72 bytes are unchanged so consumers of the earlier layout keep
  working.  Population by filesystem:
    * ext4: real inode number (meta_from_ino uses the resolved ino).
    * memfs: stable synthetic id from a process-global AtomicU64
      (NEXT_MEMFS_INO, starts at 1) assigned at node creation — gives correct
      file identity for hard-link dedup / find -inum within tmpfs.
    * FAT: first cluster (closest stable per-file id; empty files report 0).
    * devfs/procfs/sysfs/iso9660: 0 (they build FileMeta via
      ..FileMeta::minimal(), which now zero-fills ino) — pseudo/read-only
      filesystems with no stable Unix inode identity.  ISO9660 could later
      use the extent LBA if a program needs it.
  posix/src/stat.rs reads ino @72 into st_ino; statx already copies
  st_ino -> stx_ino so it benefits transitively.  services/init buffers
  bumped 72 -> 80.  2 new host tests (inode passthrough, zero=unavailable);
  17103 posix host tests pass; kernel + posix + init build clean.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) open()/openat()/openat2() with O_TMPFILE now fail with
  EOPNOTSUPP instead of silently mis-opening.  translate_open_flags ignored
  the O_TMPFILE bits entirely, so open("/tmp", O_TMPFILE|O_RDWR) stripped to
  a bare O_RDWR open of the *directory* path — the caller believed it had an
  anonymous temp file but got a directory handle (or a confusing error), and
  any write went nowhere sensible.  Linux returns EOPNOTSUPP for O_TMPFILE on
  filesystems without support, so we now do the same: a single guard in
  open() (which openat/openat2/open64/creat all funnel through) detects the
  raw __O_TMPFILE bit and returns -1/EOPNOTSUPP before issuing any syscall.
  1 new host test (open O_TMPFILE -> EOPNOTSUPP); existing openat2 phase136
  validation tests still pass (they assert errno != EINVAL; EOPNOTSUPP=95).
  17114 host tests pass; both targets build clean; no new clippy findings.
  WHY NOT WIRE SYS_FS_TMPFILE (=648)?  It exists but is itself incomplete:
  its handler creates a *visible* ".tmp_<tsc>" file that is NOT auto-deleted
  on close (handler comment contradicts the number.rs doc claiming auto-
  delete).  Wiring to it would leak visible temp files and violate O_TMPFILE
  semantics (anonymous, unlinked, auto-removed).  The musl-style fallback
  (create O_EXCL then immediately unlink, keep the fd) ALSO cannot work here:
  kernel file handles are PATH-BASED — fs::handle::read/write re-resolve
  file.path through the VFS on every call (kernel/src/fs/handle.rs:314,~333),
  so unlink severs the handle and the data becomes inaccessible.
  PROPER FIX (deferred, needs kernel work): give file handles an inode/object
  reference that survives unlink (orphan-inode support), or fix SYS_FS_TMPFILE
  to create a real anonymous inode reclaimed on last-close.  Once either
  exists, replace the EOPNOTSUPP guard in open() with a SYS_FS_TMPFILE call
  (or create+unlink) keyed on the raw __O_TMPFILE bit.  Trigger condition:
  kernel handle layer moves from path-based to inode/object-based.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) POSIX semaphores now block on the kernel futex instead
  of busy-spinning.  sem_wait spun on core::hint::spin_loop() with NO yield
  syscall (the doc even claimed "no kernel futex support yet"), so a waiter
  on an exhausted semaphore pinned a CPU core at 100% and, on a single-core
  system, could livelock the very poster it was waiting for.  The kernel has
  had SYS_FUTEX_WAIT=210 / WAKE=211 / WAIT_TIMEOUT=214 all along, and the
  semaphore counter (a 4-byte-aligned AtomicI32) is a perfect futex word.
  Fix (cfg-split, bare metal uses futex / host spins since tests never block):
    * sem_wait: fast path is a pure userspace CAS (no syscall); on exhaustion
      it calls SYS_FUTEX_WAIT(addr, observed_value) and re-loops.  The
      observed value is passed as the futex "expected" so a post that lands
      between our load and the syscall makes *word != expected and the
      kernel returns immediately (no lost wakeup).
    * sem_post: after incrementing, calls SYS_FUTEX_WAKE(addr, 1).
    * sem_timedwait: now computes the remaining ns to the deadline (i128 +
      saturating arithmetic, overflow-safe) and blocks via
      SYS_FUTEX_WAIT_TIMEOUT instead of a 1ms spin-sleep poll.
    * Stale module doc rewritten (named semaphores ARE implemented via the
      static pool — they were never ENOSYS stubs as the old header claimed).
  1 new host test (sem_wait fast-path drains a count-of-2). 17113 posix host
  tests pass; bare-metal + host build clean; no new clippy findings in the
  changed line ranges.
  DOCUMENTED LIMITATION: named semaphores live in a PER-PROCESS static pool
  (NAMED_SEMS), so two different processes that sem_open the same name get
  independent counters — there is no cross-process sharing.  The futex is
  also a private (per-address-space) futex, so even if the pool were shared
  the wake would need a shared address.  Proper cross-process named
  semaphores need the pool in named shared memory (SYS_SHM_* + a name
  registry); deferred.  Within a single multi-threaded process (the
  supported case) the futex-backed semaphore is fully correct.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) KERNEL BUG: fs::notify never delivered child events.
  Found while investigating whether to rewire posix inotify (currently
  polling-based) to the native kernel watch API (SYS_FS_WATCH_CREATE/READ/
  CLOSE = 622/623/624).  The kernel notify module (kernel/src/fs/notify.rs)
  IS wired into the VFS success paths (mkdir->emit_created, unlink->
  emit_deleted, write->emit_modified, rename->emit_renamed, chmod/chown/
  xattr->emit_metadata), so it looked like a working event source.  But the
  emit() path-matching test was broken:
      path.starts_with(&watch.path)
        && path.as_bytes().get(watch.path.len()) == Some(&b'/')
  create_watch normalizes watch.path to END WITH '/', so the byte at
  watch.path.len() is the FIRST CHARACTER OF THE CHILD NAME, never a '/'.
  Result: NO child event ever matched.  Only the `else if` branch (path IS
  the watched dir itself) fired, so the system delivered self-events but
  none of the create/delete/modify/rename events inside a watched directory
  — i.e. the primary inotify use case was dead.  The boot self_test()
  exercises child events and so was FAILING, but main.rs:885 only logs a
  WARNING (non-fatal), so it shipped silently unnoticed.
  Fix: extracted a pure `path_matches(watch_path, recursive, candidate)`
  helper using strip_suffix('/') (self event) + strip_prefix(watch_path)
  (inside; the trailing slash guarantees the separator boundary, so no
  bogus byte check) and rewrote emit()'s matcher to call it for both the
  affected path and the rename destination.  Added 8 path_matches assertions
  to self_test as a regression guard (child match, self match, grandchild
  reject non-recursive, grandchild accept recursive, prefix-sibling "/docsx"
  reject, unrelated reject, root child match, root grandchild reject).
  Kernel builds clean for x86_64-ouros; no new clippy findings in notify.rs.
  This is a prerequisite for rewiring posix inotify off polling onto the
  kernel watch API (next task) — without it the kernel API would be useless.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) posix inotify rewired from polling to the native kernel
  watch API.  Follows directly from the kernel notify fix above (now that the
  kernel is a real event source).  Previously posix::epoll implemented inotify
  by snapshotting directory listings via SYS_FS_LIST_DIR + stat on every
  read()/readiness check and diffing children — an O(entries) poll that missed
  any change reverted between two reads and could not see a content edit that
  left the file size unchanged (no-op-stub / inferior-reimplementation bug
  class, roadmap.md:1420).
  Rewrite (posix/src/epoll.rs):
    * Added SYS_FS_WATCH_CREATE/READ/CLOSE (622/623/624) + FS_WATCH_EVENT_SIZE
      (528) to posix/src/syscall.rs and to all three syscall-number test lists
      (verified against kernel/src/syscall/number.rs and the kernel handler
      layout in handlers.rs: path[0..256], new_path[256..512], watch_id
      [512..520], event_type u32 [520..524]).
    * InotifyWatch now stores {wd, mask (original inotify mask), kernel_id,
      path} — one inotify watch == one kernel watch.  Dropped the per-watch
      child-snapshot arrays, self_size/self_exists, is_dir, and
      MAX_INOTIFY_CHILDREN entirely.
    * inotify_add_watch issues SYS_FS_WATCH_CREATE with a collapsed kernel
      mask; inotify_rm_watch and inotify_instance_close issue
      SYS_FS_WATCH_CLOSE (no more leaks).  read()/is_readable() drain pending
      kernel events via SYS_FS_WATCH_READ (pump_instance/pump_one_watch).
    * Pure, host-tested translation (translate_kernel_event + relative_name):
      kernel Created->IN_CREATE(child); Deleted->IN_DELETE(child) or
      IN_DELETE_SELF+IN_IGNORED+auto-disarm(self); Modified->IN_MODIFY;
      Renamed->IN_MOVED_FROM+IN_MOVED_TO(shared cookie) or IN_MOVE_SELF(self);
      MetadataChanged->IN_ATTRIB; Accessed->IN_ACCESS; Overflow->IN_Q_OVERFLOW.
      Non-recursive (grandchildren never match), matching inotify semantics.
    * inotify_to_kernel_mask collapses all IN_MOVED_*/IN_MOVE_SELF -> RENAME
      and IN_DELETE|IN_DELETE_SELF -> DELETE; IN_OPEN/IN_CLOSE_* map to no
      kernel bit (watch is created with kernel_id==0 and is inert, accepted
      for Linux compat).  The original inotify mask is retained per-watch so
      fine-grained filtering happens on the posix side after the kernel
      coalesces.
    * 18 new host unit tests for the pure functions (relative_name self/child/
      grandchild/sibling-prefix/unrelated/root; translate create/delete-self/
      delete-child/modify/rename-pair/move-self/metadata/access/overflow/
      grandchild-ignored; mask collapsing).
  Both targets build clean (bare-metal x86_64-unknown-none and host
  x86_64-pc-windows-gnu); 111 inotify/translate/relative_name tests pass; no
  new clippy findings in the rewritten ranges (used edition-2024 let-chains to
  avoid collapsible_if/match, &slice loops to avoid explicit_iter_loop, and a
  Copy Rel enum to avoid needless_pass_by_value).  Pre-existing pedantic
  findings elsewhere in epoll.rs (and the long-but-pre-existing
  inotify_add_watch too_many_lines) were left untouched.

  KNOWN LIMITATION (kernel watch API is UTF-8-only): sys_fs_watch_create
  parses the path with core::str::from_utf8 and create_watch stores a String,
  so a watched path containing non-UTF-8 bytes is rejected by the kernel even
  though our paths are byte paths (CLAUDE.md rule 7).  posix already does the
  existence/ENOENT check on the raw bytes first, so the only affected case is
  an existing path with non-UTF-8 bytes, which currently surfaces as ENOSPC
  (the generic "kwatch_create failed" mapping).  PROPER FIX: change the kernel
  notify watch API (kernel/src/fs/notify.rs Watch.path + FsEvent.path/new_path
  and the create/read handlers) to store and compare paths as &[u8]/Vec<u8>
  instead of str/String, then plumb raw bytes through SYS_FS_WATCH_CREATE/READ.
  Deferred because it is a kernel-side change spanning notify.rs + two syscall
  handlers and the non-UTF-8-path case is rare; trigger the fix when adding
  any non-UTF-8 path support work in the fs zone.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) klogctl() wired to the kernel log ring — same no-op-stub
  bug class (roadmap.md:1420).  klogctl validated its arguments fully (Linux
  cmd-range / NULL-buf / len<0 / CONSOLE_LEVEL-range EINVAL ordering, plus the
  Phase-172 CAP_SYSLOG gate) and then returned -1/ENOSYS for EVERY data action,
  never calling the existing kernel SYS_LOG_READ (102) — which already reads
  the JSON-lines ring buffer and returns (entry_count, newest_seq).
  Fix:
    * Added SYS_LOG_READ=102 + a syscall3_2ret wrapper (captures rax+rdx, i.e.
      value+value2) to posix/src/syscall.rs and to the nonzero/unique/range
      syscall-number test lists.
    * unistd.rs klogctl now dispatches: CLOSE/OPEN -> 0 (Linux no-ops; were
      wrongly ENOSYS); READ -> consuming read via a per-process KLOG_READ_CURSOR
      (advanced by newest_seq); READ_ALL -> non-consuming read from
      KLOG_CLEAR_FLOOR; READ_CLEAR -> READ_ALL then advance both cursors past
      everything currently buffered; CLEAR -> advance both cursors (drain to
      find true newest); SIZE_UNREAD -> bytes available since the read cursor;
      SIZE_BUFFER -> bytes currently buffered since the clear floor.  Byte
      counts are derived by scanning the kernel's JSON-lines output for the
      count-th '\n' (klog_json_lines_len); aggregate queries drain into a 2 KiB
      scratch (klog_drain).  cfg-split: host returns an empty log (0).
    * CONSOLE_OFF/CONSOLE_ON/CONSOLE_LEVEL remain ENOSYS — no kernel syscall
      sets the serial log level yet (klog::set_serial_level is unexposed).
    * Rewrote ~20 host tests that pinned the old validate-then-ENOSYS stub
      (close/open now 0; clear/size/read now succeed with 0 on the empty host
      log; CONSOLE_* still ENOSYS; cap-gate EPERM tests unchanged).  Full posix
      suite green (17133 host tests); both targets build clean; no new clippy
      findings in the changed ranges.

  ## Judgment Calls (klogctl emulation over a non-consuming seq-cursor API):
    * The READ cursor and clear floor are PER-PROCESS atomics, not the global
      kernel state Linux's syslog uses.  Each process gets an independent view;
      a "clear" in one process does not affect another.  This is fine for the
      dmesg/journald read paths but differs from Linux's shared consuming read.
    * "Clear" is EMULATED by hiding entries at/below a stored seq floor — the
      kernel has no log-clear syscall and the ring is non-consuming, so the
      entries still physically exist (and are still visible to other processes
      / a fresh process).  PROPER FIX if true clearing is needed: add a kernel
      SYS_LOG_CLEAR (and/or per-reader consuming cursors) to klog.rs.
    * A truncated READ_ALL returns the OLDEST entries that fit (the kernel
      reads oldest->newest and stops when the buffer fills); Linux returns the
      NEWEST that fit.  Acceptable while the ring (256 entries) is small.
    * SIZE_BUFFER reports currently-buffered bytes, not the ring's fixed byte
      capacity (the kernel does not expose capacity).  This is what dmesg
      actually needs (it sizes its READ_ALL buffer from it); a tiny race exists
      if entries arrive between SIZE_BUFFER and READ_ALL.  PROPER FIX: expose
      ring capacity via SYS_LOG_READ (e.g. a query mode) if a caller needs the
      true capacity.
  These are easy to reverse (all confined to klogctl + the two cursors).

- (DONE 2026-05-30) lseek() SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE wired to the kernel — same
  no-op-stub bug class.  lseek rejected whence == SEEK_DATA(3) / SEEK_HOLE(4)
  with EINVAL ("whence is not a valid value") even though the kernel fully
  implements SYS_FS_SEEK_DATA=650 / SYS_FS_SEEK_HOLE=651 (handle+offset ->
  resulting position, backed by fs::handle::seek with SeekFrom::Data/Hole).
  Net effect before the fix: sparse-aware tools — cp --sparse=auto, GNU tar,
  rsync -S, qemu-img, and anything that walks data/hole extents to skip large
  zero regions — got a spurious EINVAL and silently fell back to dense copies
  (or failed), wasting space and bandwidth on sparse files.
    * Added SYS_FS_SEEK_DATA/SYS_FS_SEEK_HOLE to posix syscall.rs (+ all three
      syscall test lists, within the 600..800 FS range).
    * lseek (file.rs): SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE now pass whence validation; for
      HandleKind::File they dispatch syscall2(SYS_FS_SEEK_DATA/HOLE, handle,
      offset); other whence values keep SYS_FS_SEEK.  Negative offset with
      SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE is rejected with EINVAL (an absolute start offset
      cast to u64 would otherwise become a huge position).  Non-File kinds
      still return ESPIPE.  lseek64 delegates to lseek, so it inherits the fix.
    * 4 new host tests (SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE accepted, negative-offset EINVAL
      for each).  17112 posix host tests pass; bare-metal + host posix build
      clean; no new clippy findings in the lseek line range.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) flock() wired to the kernel advisory-lock table — same
  no-op-stub bug class.  flock was a validate-then-return-0 stub ("our kernel
  does not yet enforce advisory locks") even though the kernel fully
  implements SYS_FS_FLOCK=609 / SYS_FS_FUNLOCK=640 backed by a per-path,
  owner-keyed lock table (Vfs::flock/funlock/funlock_all).  A no-op flock
  provides ZERO mutual exclusion, so every program relying on lock files
  (package managers, dpkg/apt-style tools, single-instance daemons, mail
  spools) silently raced.
    * Added SYS_FS_FLOCK/SYS_FS_FUNLOCK to posix syscall.rs (+ all three
      syscall test lists).
    * Bare-metal do_flock worker (file.rs): fd -> path via
      fdtable::get_fd_path, owner = getpid (SYS_PROCESS_ID); LOCK_UN ->
      SYS_FS_FUNLOCK; LOCK_SH/LOCK_EX -> SYS_FS_FLOCK (type 0/1).  LOCK_NB
      maps WouldBlock -> EWOULDBLOCK; blocking mode polls with SYS_SLEEP(0)
      yields between retries.  Host build stays validation-only (returns 0).
    * KERNEL FIX (proc/pcb.rs destroy_process_resources): now calls
      Vfs::funlock_all(pid) on process teardown.  Previously a process that
      died holding a lock leaked it forever (every other waiter on that path
      would block until reboot) — funlock_all existed but was only called
      from tests.  This makes flock safe to actually use.
  17108 posix host tests pass; bare-metal + host posix and kernel build
  clean; the one new clippy finding (bool_to_int_with_if) was fixed.
  JUDGMENT CALLS / DOCUMENTED LIMITATIONS:
    1. Path-less descriptors (pipes, sockets, anonymous fds) are accepted as
       a no-op: Linux locks the open file description's inode, but our kernel
       lock table is keyed by resolved path and cannot represent them.
    2. Blocking flock (no LOCK_NB) polls with a yield rather than truly
       blocking, because SYS_FS_FLOCK is non-blocking.  A real blocking wait
       needs a kernel wait queue / wake-on-release; deferred.
    3. flock locks are owned by the PID (process scope), not per-OFD as on
       Linux.  All threads/dup'd fds in a process share one lock per path.
       Closer per-OFD semantics would need an OFD identifier in the ABI.
    4. lockf() is STILL a no-op (intentionally NOT wired): it locks byte
       RANGES, but the kernel lock table is whole-file only.  Mapping lockf
       onto whole-file locks would turn independent ranges (e.g. a database
       locking distinct records) into false contention / deadlock — strictly
       worse than the no-op.  F_TEST also has no non-destructive kernel query
       syscall.  Proper lockf needs kernel byte-range locks + a query
       syscall; tracked here as a follow-up.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) sync()/syncfs() wired to the kernel global flush — same
  no-op-stub bug class.  Both were pure no-ops justified by "filesystem
  writes are synchronous", yet fsync(2) already issues SYS_FS_SYNC=641 (a
  real journal/page-cache flush), so the "synchronous" claim was false and
  sync(8)/`sync()`/syncfs(2) never actually flushed anything to storage.
  Fix (cfg-split, matching statvfs/utimes): bare metal issues syscall0(
  SYS_FS_SYNC); host build stays a validation-only no-op so the existing
  host tests (test_sync_no_crash, test_syncfs_succeeds, the EBADF cases)
  still hold.  syncfs keeps its fd validation (EBADF on negative/closed fd)
  then issues the same global sync.  NOTE: our SYS_FS_SYNC flushes every
  mounted filesystem rather than just the one containing the fd — a valid
  superset of the syncfs(2)/sync(2) guarantee.  17108 posix host tests pass;
  bare-metal + host posix build clean.  Also: completed the <sys/xattr.h>
  re-export surface (llistxattr/flistxattr/lremovexattr/fremovexattr were
  missing) and gated the host-dead KERNEL_STATVFS_LEN const to silence a
  build warning.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) xattr family (getxattr/setxattr/listxattr/removexattr +
  l*/f* variants, 12 functions) wired to the kernel — same no-op-stub bug
  class.  All twelve were ENOTSUP stubs ("our filesystem does not support
  extended attributes yet") even though the kernel fully implements
  SYS_FS_GET_XATTR=633 / SET_XATTR=634 / REMOVE_XATTR=635 / LIST_XATTRS=636
  and ext4 stores inline + external xattrs (the ext4 self-test exercises
  set/get/list/remove).  Net effect before the fix: setfattr/getfattr,
  `tar --xattrs`, file capabilities, ACLs, and SELinux/security contexts all
  silently reported "not supported".
    * Added the four SYS_FS_*_XATTR constants to posix syscall.rs (+ the
      three syscall test lists).
    * Bare-metal workers do_getxattr/do_setxattr/do_listxattr/do_removexattr
      in xattr.rs: resolve the path (or fd→path via fdtable::get_fd_path),
      issue syscall3/4/5, errno::translate on negative return.
    * getxattr/listxattr honour POSIX size semantics: a size-0 call is a
      size query, and a non-zero-but-too-small buffer yields ERANGE (the
      kernel now returns the TRUE length — see the kernel ABI fix below).
    * setxattr honours XATTR_CREATE/XATTR_REPLACE via a pre-existence probe
      (the kernel SET_XATTR carries no flags): CREATE→EEXIST if present,
      REPLACE→ENODATA if absent.  Conflicting/unknown flags → EINVAL.
    * KERNEL ABI FIX (handlers.rs only — Vfs::get_xattr/list_xattrs callers
      are just the syscall path + the ext4 self-test which calls Vfs::
      directly, so safe): sys_fs_get_xattr and sys_fs_list_xattrs now accept
      capacity==0 (size query) instead of rejecting it as EINVAL, and return
      the TRUE value/list length rather than the truncated copy length, so
      callers can size-query and detect truncation.  list_xattrs only packs
      when the whole list fits (no ambiguous partial fill).
  17108 posix host tests pass (37 xattr tests rewritten for the new
  validation surface); bare-metal + host posix and kernel builds clean.
  JUDGMENT CALLS / DOCUMENTED LIMITATIONS:
    1. lgetxattr/lsetxattr/llistxattr/lremovexattr do NOT honour no-follow:
       the kernel xattr syscalls resolve with resolve_follow, so on a symlink
       they operate on the target.  Same root cause/fix as the lchown and
       utimensat AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW limitations (needs a no-follow ABI).
    2. A missing attribute reports ENOENT, not the Linux-conventional
       ENODATA, because the kernel collapses "file not found" and "attribute
       not found" into KernelError::NotFound.  Distinguishing them needs a
       dedicated kernel error variant; deferred (low value — most callers
       treat any error from getxattr as "absent").
    3. setxattr's CREATE/REPLACE pre-check is a separate syscall from the
       set, so there is a benign TOCTOU window.  The only proper fix is to
       add a flags arg to the kernel SET_XATTR syscall; deferred.

- (DONE 2026-05-30) chmod/fchmod/chown/fchown/lchown wired to the kernel
  (same no-op-stub bug class as the utimes family).  All five were validate-
  then-return-0 stubs ("No permission system yet — accept silently") even
  though the kernel fully implements SYS_FS_SET_PERMS=631 and
  SYS_FS_SET_OWNER=630 (ext4/memfs set_permissions/set_owner exist and stamp
  ctime; FAT correctly returns NotSupported).  Net effect before the fix:
  `chmod`, `install -m`, `tar -p` mode/owner restore, and any chown/chmod
  silently did nothing on a real fs.  Fix mirrors the utimes cfg-split:
    * Added SYS_FS_SET_OWNER=630 / SYS_FS_SET_PERMS=631 to posix syscall.rs
      (+ to the non-zero, uniqueness, and fs-range syscall test lists).
    * Bare-metal helpers set_perms_path (resolve_or_err + syscall3
      SYS_FS_SET_PERMS, mode masked to 0o7777) and set_owner_path
      (resolve_or_err + syscall4 SYS_FS_SET_OWNER), errno::translate on
      negative return.
    * The five entry points keep all existing validation + the CAP_CHOWN
      gate, then on target_os="none" issue the syscall.  fd-based
      fchmod/fchown resolve the fd to its stored path via
      fdtable::get_fd_path (path-less fds like pipes succeed as a no-op).
      A chown/fchown/lchown that changes neither field (both args u32::MAX)
      short-circuits to success without a syscall (no spurious ctime bump).
      Host builds keep returning 0 after validation.
    * KERNEL FIX: Vfs::set_owner now honours the POSIX (uid_t)-1/(gid_t)-1
      "leave unchanged" sentinel.  Previously it wrote both uid and gid
      unconditionally, so chown(path, -1, gid) would have clobbered the uid
      with 0xFFFFFFFF.  Vfs::set_owner now resolves u32::MAX fields against
      the file's current owner (via Vfs::metadata) before dispatching, so
      every backing fs impl still receives concrete values.  Handler doc
      updated to document the sentinel.
  17114 posix host tests pass; bare-metal + host posix build clean; kernel
  build clean.
  JUDGMENT CALLS / DOCUMENTED LIMITATIONS:
    1. lchown follows symlinks: the kernel SYS_FS_SET_OWNER (Vfs::set_owner)
       resolves with resolve_follow, so lchown on a symlink changes the
       TARGET's owner, not the link's.  Correct for the common non-symlink
       case.  Same root cause and proper fix as the utimensat
       AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW limitation below (needs a no-follow kernel ABI).
