##      table; this is fine since we always return EBADF before
##      any option-specific path runs.
##  54. EVENTFD / EVENTFD2 / FUTEX_WAITV / PKEY_ALLOC /
##      PKEY_FREE / PKEY_MPROTECT / GET_ROBUST_LIST /
##      SET_MEMPOLICY_HOME_NODE — 8 syscalls DONE as
##      input-validated principled-errno stubs.
##         - eventfd: legacy form, flags must be 0; ENOSYS.
##         - eventfd2: accept SEMAPHORE|CLOEXEC|NONBLOCK only;
##           ENOSYS so userspace event loops fall back to pipes.
##         - futex_waitv: validate nr ∈ 1..=128, flags == 0,
##           waiters ptr + 24B-per-entry buffer + optional 16B
##           timespec + clockid ∈ {CLOCK_REALTIME, CLOCK_MONOTONIC};
##           ENOSYS so glibc falls back to iterated FUTEX_WAIT.
##         - pkey_alloc / pkey_free / pkey_mprotect: MPK
##           protection keys.  PKU not enabled in our kernel;
##           pkey_alloc validates flags + access_rights bits then
##           ENOSYS (== "MPK unavailable" to glibc).  pkey_free
##           returns EINVAL for any in-range key (no keys
##           allocated).  pkey_mprotect with pkey == -1 forwards
##           to plain mprotect (default key); in-range pkey
##           returns EINVAL (no key allocated); out-of-range
##           returns EINVAL.
##         - get_robust_list: validate non-negative pid + non-NULL
##           head_ptr + len_ptr (both writable u64); return ENOSYS.
##           glibc treats ENOSYS as "no robust list registered"
##           and skips the cleanup pass.
##         - set_mempolicy_home_node: validate home_node == 0
##           (only one NUMA node), flags == 0, len > 0, addr
##           aligned to 16 KiB; return ENOSYS so callers fall
##           back to plain MBIND policy.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * eventfd ENOSYS rather than fake fd: userspace event
##           loops (libuv, tokio uring, glib) detect ENOSYS and
##           use pipe2 as the fallback wakeup mechanism, which
##           we DO implement.  Returning a fake fd would leak
##           because nothing would read it.
##         * futex_waitv ENOSYS lets glibc's pthread cancellation
##           multi-wait path degrade to single-waiter loops;
##           we'd need real multi-futex queueing to implement it
##           correctly.
##         * pkey ENOSYS/EINVAL exactly matches Linux running
##           with PKU disabled in BIOS — every userspace MPK
##           caller already handles this case (it's the common
##           configuration on older CPUs).
##         * get_robust_list ENOSYS rather than 0-zero output:
##           we can't write 0 to head/len without a user-context
##           copy_to_user, and ENOSYS is the documented "feature
##           absent" answer that glibc handles.
##      Limitation: real eventfd, real futex_waitv multi-wait,
##      and real MPK support are all needed eventually.  eventfd
##      is the highest priority because it's the standard
##      wakeup primitive for io_uring completion notifications
##      and for tokio-style runtimes; futex_waitv is needed for
##      glibc-2.34+ pthread cancellation latency; MPK is needed
##      only for hardened userspace (Chromium, OpenSSL FIPS) and
##      can wait until we expose PKU CPUID.  Also: fixed an
##      existing bug where EVENTFD was defined as 290 (collision
##      with EVENTFD2); legacy eventfd is syscall 284.
##  55. Legacy x86 + kexec + mount-query + LSM family
##      (MODIFY_LDT / IOPL / IOPERM / SET_THREAD_AREA /
##      GET_THREAD_AREA / KEXEC_LOAD / KEXEC_FILE_LOAD /
##      STATMOUNT / LISTMOUNT / LSM_GET_SELF_ATTR /
##      LSM_SET_SELF_ATTR / LSM_LIST_MODULES) — 12 syscalls
##      DONE as input-validated principled-errno stubs.
##         - modify_ldt: validate func ∈ {0, 1, 2, 0x11},
##           bytecount >= 16 for writes; return ENOSYS
##           (x86_64 long mode doesn't use LDT for userspace;
##           Wine uses modify_ldt for 16/32-bit segmented code).
##         - iopl: validate level ∈ 0..=3; return EPERM
##           (direct I/O port access not granted — drivers run
##           as IPC servers behind capabilities).
##         - ioperm: validate range fits in 0..=0xFFFF; EPERM.
##         - set_thread_area / get_thread_area: validate 16B
##           user_desc; return ENOSYS (x86_64 uses
##           arch_prctl(ARCH_SET_FS) for TLS).
##         - kexec_load: validate nr_segments <= 16, segments
##           ptr required when nr>0, 32B kexec_segment per
##           entry; EPERM.
##         - kexec_file_load: validate fds (initrd_fd == -1
##           ok), cmdline ptr when len > 0; EPERM.
##         - statmount: validate 24B mnt_id_req in, output
##           writable, bufsize > 0, flags == 0; return ENOENT
##           (every mnt_id is unknown — no mount tree yet).
##         - listmount: same validation; ENOENT.
##         - lsm_get_self_attr: validate attr ∈ 100..=105
##           (CURRENT/EXEC/FSCREATE/KEYCREATE/PREV/SOCKCREATE),
##           size* read+write, flags ∈ {0, LSM_FLAG_SINGLE};
##           return EOPNOTSUPP (no LSM stacked).
##         - lsm_set_self_attr: validate attr, ctx ptr+len,
##           flags == 0; EOPNOTSUPP.
##         - lsm_list_modules: validate size* read+write,
##           flags == 0; EOPNOTSUPP.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * ENOSYS for modify_ldt/thread_area: x86 legacy paths;
##           ENOSYS is the universal "this arch lacks them"
##           signal that Wine/dosemu/glibc-32 handle by
##           switching to long-mode paths.
##         * EPERM for iopl/ioperm/kexec: not "feature absent"
##           but "you can't have this privilege" — matches
##           non-root Linux.  Returning ENOSYS would let
##           sandbox escapes think the syscall doesn't exist
##           when it's actually a security boundary.
##         * ENOENT for statmount/listmount: matches "you
##           asked about an unknown mnt_id".  Returning ENOSYS
##           would force fallback paths even once we have a
##           real mount tree.
##         * EOPNOTSUPP for LSM: documents "this build lacks
##           the feature" without claiming we lack the syscall.
##      Limitation: none of these are particularly important.
##      iopl/ioperm could matter if we host DOSBox-style
##      emulators (we'll need a capability-checked port-grant
##      then).  LSM stacking unlikely because we have a
##      different security model (capabilities + namespaces).
##      statmount/listmount need real backing once VFS mount
##      tree exists (mount is also EPERM today).
##  56. SETTIMEOFDAY / MINCORE / MREMAP / FALLOCATE / MLOCK2 /
##      ACCT / USTAT — 7 syscalls DONE as input-validated
##      principled-errno stubs.  (Note: NICE is NOT an x86_64
##      syscall — glibc implements nice() as a
##      setpriority(PRIO_PROCESS) wrapper, so no NICE constant.)
##         - settimeofday: validate 16B timeval + optional 8B
##           timezone; return EPERM.  Tools that need to set
##           the wall clock fall back to adjtimex which we
##           handle.
##         - mincore: validate addr 16 KiB aligned, length,
##           vec ptr writable for ceil(length/16K) bytes, addr
##           span readable in user space (ENOMEM if not).
##           Return ENOSYS — we don't track resident-vs-swapped
##           state because we don't swap; glibc/libgc callers
##           assume "all resident" on ENOSYS which is correct.
##         - mremap: validate old_addr 16 KiB aligned, new_size
##           > 0, flags ∈ {MAYMOVE, FIXED, DONTUNMAP},
##           cross-flag constraints (FIXED requires MAYMOVE +
##           aligned new_addr; DONTUNMAP requires MAYMOVE +
##           old_size == new_size).  Return ENOMEM — Linux's
##           "no room to grow without MAYMOVE" answer; glibc
##           malloc handles ENOMEM by mmap+memcpy+munmap.
##         - fallocate: validate fd, offset >= 0, len > 0,
##           mode flag bits (KEEP_SIZE|PUNCH_HOLE|COLLAPSE_RANGE|
##           ZERO_RANGE|INSERT_RANGE|UNSHARE_RANGE), PUNCH_HOLE
##           requires KEEP_SIZE; return EOPNOTSUPP so sqlite /
##           PostgreSQL WAL fall back to manual zero-writes.
##         - mlock2: validate flags ∈ {0, MLOCK_ONFAULT}, range
##           readable; return 0 (no swap → all memory locked).
##         - acct: validate optional path (NUL-terminated);
##           return EPERM (CAP_SYS_PACCT not exposed).
##         - ustat: validate 32B ustat output buffer; return
##           ENOSYS (deprecated since Linux 2.6, removed from
##           glibc 2.28; callers fall back to statfs which we
##           handle).
##      Choice rationale:
##         * EPERM for settimeofday matches non-root Linux;
##           every NTP/hwclock tool already handles "can't set
##           clock without privilege" by reporting the offset
##           through adjtimex.
##         * ENOSYS for mincore is friendlier than EINVAL
##           because every caller has an "assume all resident"
##           fallback that is exactly what we need.
##         * ENOMEM for mremap (not ENOSYS): mremap exists,
##           we just can't grow in place.  glibc malloc, jemalloc,
##           and tcmalloc all have an ENOMEM → mmap+memcpy
##           path.  Returning ENOSYS would force them onto a
##           slower path that probes for "does mremap work at
##           all" once per process.
##         * EOPNOTSUPP for fallocate matches "ext2 / tmpfs
##           don't support fallocate", which is what every
##           database engine handles gracefully.
##         * Success for mlock2 matches non-swapping kernels
##           (the memory is already locked); we accept the call
##           without doing anything.
##         * EPERM for acct because process accounting is a
##           privileged operation.
##         * Also fixed: the MREMAP constant existed (since an
##           older batch) but was never wired into dispatch —
##           it was silently ENOSYS.  Now properly dispatched.
##      Limitation: mincore is the most-likely future TODO —
##      libgc and glibc malloc trim heuristics call mincore to
##      decide when to release pages back to the kernel.  We
##      return ENOSYS so they skip the heuristic.  If we ever
##      implement page-out (we don't plan to), real mincore
##      becomes relevant.  mremap real implementation is
##      bounded by needing reservation-tracking in mm/ — we
##      have the data structures for it; just not the
##      mremap interface itself.  Fallocate punching for sparse
##      files needs VFS hole-support which we don't have yet.

##  57. PREAD64 / PWRITE64 / GETCWD / CHDIR / FCHDIR — 5 syscalls
##      DONE as input-validated principled stubs.  Also added FCHDIR
##      to the syscall-number table (it was missing; CHDIR=80 was
##      present but FCHDIR=81 was not).
##         - pread64 / pwrite64: validate fd, non-negative offset,
##           buf range (writable for read, readable for write);
##           return ENOSYS.  Rationale: the VFS doesn't yet have a
##           positional-I/O backend.  Returning ENOSYS makes glibc
##           fall back to lseek+read+lseek (preserving offset for
##           the caller).
##         - getcwd: validate buf non-NULL + writable, size >= 2;
##           write "/\0" via copy_to_user and return 2 (the Linux
##           contract: bytes-written including NUL).  CRITICAL: this
##           is called by every libc startup, every shell's prompt,
##           every config-file loader.  Returning ENOSYS would
##           break bash, dash, busybox, glibc init.  Returning "/"
##           is the only consistent answer until per-process cwd
##           tracking exists, because chdir() (see below) is also a
##           no-op.
##         - chdir: validate path NUL-terminated; return 0.
##           Silent success; observable cwd via getcwd remains "/".
##           Consistent with the kernel never having moved.
##         - fchdir: validate fd; return 0.  Same semantics as
##           chdir, dirfd-keyed.
##      Limitation / future work: the kernel does NOT track a
##      per-process cwd at all.  kernel/src/proc/ has zero
##      references to cwd / current_dir / working_dir; the VFS
##      resolves paths against an implicit root (see comment at
##      linux.rs ~696 "Our VFS resolves paths against the caller's
##      cwd unconditionally" — which is currently a lie, since
##      there is no cwd).  This needs a follow-on task to add
##      cwd to the PCB (process control block), wire chdir/fchdir
##      to update it, wire getcwd to read it, and wire every
##      relative-path lookup in the VFS to consult it.  Tracking
##      that as a separate item in the roadmap (kernel-process).
##      Bug noted in batch 31: tools that rely on chdir-then-spawn
##      to set the child's cwd will silently behave as if every
##      child starts at "/".  This affects shell pipelines that
##      use `cd dir; cmd` semantics and Makefiles that expect to
##      run rules relative to a sub-directory.  Acceptable for
##      now because there is no real shell using these syscalls
##      yet — the kernel-internal shell uses VFS APIs directly.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * ENOSYS for pread/pwrite (not EOPNOTSUPP) because the
##           syscalls exist on every Linux but the kernel's lack of
##           positional-I/O is exactly "this syscall is not present"
##           — and glibc treats ENOSYS as the cue to fall back to
##           the seek+rw+seek emulation that we want.
##         * "/" for getcwd, not "/unknown" or "/.": every test
##           harness that compares basename(getcwd()) to a literal
##           string (which is most of them) expects "/" to mean
##           root, while anything starting with "/." is treated as
##           hidden by ls -A and confuses GNU make's $(CURDIR).
##         * 0 (silent success) for chdir/fchdir, not -ENOSYS:
##           every dynamic linker / startup runtime calls chdir
##           once on receipt of an argv with a relative-path
##           script-loader; -ENOSYS would break dynamic linking
##           on day one.

##  58. FLOCK / GETDENTS / GETDENTS64 / WAITID / PREADV / PWRITEV /
##      PREADV2 / PWRITEV2 — 8 syscalls DONE as input-validated
##      principled stubs.  All eight had no constant defined before
##      this batch.  Sets cover advisory file-locking, directory
##      iteration, modern wait variants, and positional vectored
##      I/O — the most-impactful remaining gaps in the Linux fd
##      surface from the find_gaps.py audit (36 → 28 missing).
##         - flock: validate fd, op ∈ {LOCK_SH=1, LOCK_EX=2,
##           LOCK_UN=8} with optional LOCK_NB=4 modifier; return 0.
##           Advisory locks are by definition no-ops in
##           single-task scenarios; the single-task simplification
##           is semantically safe (Linux flock is advisory — only
##           cooperating programs observe it).  Multi-process
##           coordination is a separate follow-up (see below).
##         - getdents / getdents64: validate fd, dirp writable,
##           count; return ENOSYS.  getdents (legacy 32-bit) is
##           glibc-removed since 2.x.  getdents64 returning ENOSYS
##           keeps readdir() returning NULL+errno=ENOSYS, which
##           glibc treats consistently as "this kernel cannot
##           iterate" — returning 0 (empty dir) would be a worse
##           lie because programs would silently fail to find
##           anything.
##         - waitid: validate idtype ∈ {P_ALL, P_PID, P_PGID,
##           P_PIDFD}, options mask (WNOHANG|WSTOPPED|WEXITED|
##           WCONTINUED|WNOWAIT), require at least one event class,
##           validate optional 128B siginfo_t + 144B rusage
##           outputs.  Return 0 on WNOHANG (no state change),
##           ECHILD otherwise (no children to wait on).  Glibc's
##           posix_spawn falls back to wait4 cleanly on ECHILD.
##         - preadv / pwritev / preadv2 / pwritev2: validate fd,
##           non-negative offset (preadv2/pwritev2 allow -1 to
##           mean "use file offset"), iov array readable, every
##           iovec.base+len satisfying the requested access, flags
##           in the RWF_HIPRI|DSYNC|SYNC|NOWAIT|APPEND|NOAPPEND|
##           ATOMIC|DONTCACHE mask.  Return ENOSYS so glibc falls
##           back to lseek + readv + lseek.  RWF_* unknown bits
##           are EOPNOTSUPP (Linux's documented "kernel doesn't
##           support this RWF_ flag" answer).
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Success for flock matches the single-task case
##           exactly: in the absence of any contender, every
##           cooperative caller successfully grabs the lock.
##         * ENOSYS (not 0/empty) for getdents64 because callers
##           must distinguish "kernel can't list" from "empty dir"
##           or they make wrong inferences (e.g., `rm -rf` would
##           skip non-empty directories that report empty).
##         * waitid's ECHILD-when-blocking is the right answer
##           for a task with no children: a real Linux process
##           with no children waiting on P_ALL gets ECHILD; we
##           reach that exact state because no kernel-context
##           task has children either.
##         * EOPNOTSUPP for unknown RWF_* bits matches Linux's
##           contract — it's how callers feature-detect new bits.
##      Added a `validate_iov` helper that mirrors the iteration
##      done by sys_readv / sys_writev (each iovec entry: read 16B
##      from iov_ptr, validate base/len against read or write
##      permission).  Shared across all four positional vectored
##      syscalls; saves ~120 lines of duplicated validation.
##      Limitation / future work:
##         * Real flock requires per-inode lock state shared
##           across processes.  Today two processes both observe
##           "lock granted" simultaneously.  Documented because
##           this matters for vim/emacs/git lockfiles when we
##           eventually run two userspace processes against the
##           same filesystem.  Adding a real flock table needs an
##           ino-keyed map in the VFS plus wait-queues for blocked
##           waiters.
##         * Real getdents64 requires VFS directory iteration:
##           an opendir-style cursor stored alongside the fd, an
##           emit_dirent helper that packs `struct linux_dirent64`
##           records up to `count` bytes, and short-read semantics
##           for partial buffers.  Tracked separately because the
##           VFS itself doesn't yet expose iter_dir; this is one
##           of the bigger "real impl" items in the Linux ABI
##           backlog and unblocks `ls`, `find`, shell glob
##           expansion, and Python `os.listdir`.
##         * Real preadv/pwritev/preadv2/pwritev2 just need the
##           positional-I/O backend that pread/pwrite need (see
##           item 57).  Once one lands, the vectored variants are
##           trivial loops over readv/writev.
##         * waitid going through the real reaping path: today
##           wait4 has the proper reap logic; waitid would need to
##           translate idtype/options into the same lookup +
##           write `siginfo_t { si_signo=SIGCHLD, si_code,
##           si_pid, si_uid, si_status, si_utime, si_stime }`.
##           Mechanical, just not done yet.

##  59. REMAP_FILE_PAGES / IOPRIO_SET / IOPRIO_GET / IO_PGETEVENTS /
##      MOUNT_SETATTR / FCHMODAT2 / FUTEX_WAKE / FUTEX_WAIT /
##      FUTEX_REQUEUE — 9 syscalls DONE as input-validated
##      principled stubs.  None had a constant defined before this
##      batch.  Brings the constant-undispatched count to 0 again
##      and covers the next wave of genuinely-callable gaps.
##         - remap_file_pages: validate 16 KiB-aligned addr, prot
##           bits (PROT_READ|WRITE|EXEC|SEM|GROWSDOWN|GROWSUP);
##           return ENOSYS.  Deprecated since Linux 3.16 — every
##           modern caller uses MAP_FIXED mmap or mremap instead.
##         - ioprio_set: validate which ∈ {PROCESS, PGRP, USER},
##           class ∈ 0..=3, data ∈ 0..=7; return 0 (silent
##           success — we don't run a per-task I/O scheduler).
##           ionice ignores its setting cleanly.
##         - ioprio_get: validate which; return (BE << 13) | 4 —
##           the stock-Linux default.
##         - io_pgetevents: validate min<=nr, events writable,
##           timespec/sigset readable; return EINVAL (no AIO ctx
##           can exist because io_setup is ENOSYS — Linux's
##           "unknown ctx" answer).
##         - mount_setattr: validate flags ⊆ {AT_RECURSIVE,
##           NO_AUTOMOUNT, SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW, EMPTY_PATH}, attr
##           pointer, 32B mount_attr struct; return ENOSYS.
##         - fchmodat2: validate flags ⊆ {SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW,
##           EMPTY_PATH}; forward to sys_fchmodat (returns EROFS).
##           Useful immediately when Linux 6.6+ glibc bypasses
##           fchmodat and goes straight to fchmodat2 to honour
##           AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW for chmod on a symlink.
##         - futex_wake / futex_wait / futex_requeue: futex2 API
##           added in Linux 6.7.  Validate uaddr readable, flags
##           ⊆ {PRIVATE, SIZE_U32, NUMA}, clockid 0..=12 for
##           futex_wait, futex_waitv-array readable for
##           futex_requeue; return ENOSYS so glibc falls back to
##           classic futex(FUTEX_WAIT/WAKE) which we DO handle.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Silent 0 for ioprio_set because the entire purpose
##           of ionice is to express a preference — a kernel
##           with no I/O scheduler is free to ignore it (and
##           every BFQ/CFQ-less Linux config does exactly this).
##         * (BE << 13) | 4 for ioprio_get matches `cat
##           /proc/$$/io` on stock Linux when nothing has been
##           set.  Programs that check `ionice -p` see the
##           expected default and don't panic.
##         * EINVAL for io_pgetevents (not ENOSYS) because the
##           syscall exists — we just have no contexts.  Programs
##           that probe for AIO support via io_setup get ENOSYS
##           and never reach io_pgetevents; programs that did set
##           up a context elsewhere (impossible today) and pass
##           it to io_pgetevents get the truthful "no such ctx".
##         * EROFS for fchmodat2 valid: forwarding to fchmodat
##           preserves the existing "the filesystem is read-only"
##           contract.  Once a writable FS lands, both fchmodat
##           and fchmodat2 light up at once.
##         * ENOSYS for futex2: the new ABI is rarely used today
##           (futex2 is opt-in; glibc still defaults to classic
##           futex).  Returning ENOSYS makes feature-detection
##           probes work correctly.
##      Limitation / future work:
##         * ioprio could become real once an I/O scheduler is
##           wired in — store the per-task class/data and consult
##           it from the block-layer dispatch.
##         * mount_setattr blocks on the fs-API mutation path
##           which itself needs the new fsmount infrastructure.
##         * fchmodat2's AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW difference vs.
##           fchmodat doesn't matter until we have writable
##           filesystems with symlinks.
##         * futex2 promotion: at minimum, glibc 2.42+ may start
##           preferring futex2 for new locks.  Wiring this to the
##           classic futex impl (per-op translation) is a one-day
##           task once the new ABI sees real-world traction.

##  60. CREAT / USELIB / SYSFS / VHANGUP / _SYSCTL / CREATE_MODULE /
##      GET_KERNEL_SYMS / QUERY_MODULE / NFSSERVCTL / GETPMSG /
##      PUTPMSG / AFS_SYSCALL / TUXCALL / SECURITY / LOOKUP_DCOOKIE /
##      EPOLL_CTL_OLD / EPOLL_WAIT_OLD / VSERVER / FUTIMESAT —
##      19 legacy / deprecated / never-implemented syscalls DONE.
##      Brings the constants-undispatched count to zero and
##      eliminates every gap in the find_gaps.py audit.
##         - creat: forward to open_common with O_WRONLY|O_CREAT|
##           O_TRUNC.  Real callers see the same EROFS / EFAULT
##           behaviour as open().
##         - uselib / _sysctl: validate args, return ENOSYS.
##           Both are removed-from-upstream relics; our ENOSYS
##           matches what every running Linux ≥ 5.5 / glibc 2.23+
##           reports.
##         - sysfs: validate option ∈ {1,2,3}, return ENOSYS.
##           Replaced by /proc/filesystems since the 2.4 era.
##         - vhangup: return EPERM (privileged terminal reset).
##         - futimesat: validate path + 32B times[2]; return
##           ENOSYS so glibc uses utimensat (which we handle).
##         - create_module, get_kernel_syms, query_module,
##           nfsservctl, getpmsg, putpmsg, afs_syscall, tuxcall,
##           security, lookup_dcookie, epoll_ctl_old,
##           epoll_wait_old, vserver: permanent-ENOSYS upstream
##           too.  Wiring them explicitly distinguishes "known
##           defunct" from "unimplemented" — useful for strace
##           output clarity once we ship a strace.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * EPERM (not ENOSYS) for vhangup because the syscall
##           genuinely exists on every Linux and gates on
##           CAP_SYS_TTY_CONFIG.  Programs that handle "no
##           permission" gracefully (every userspace init except
##           the real one) work correctly.
##         * Forwarding creat to open_common (not stubbing
##           directly) keeps the EROFS contract consistent and
##           lights up automatically once writable FS lands.
##         * Permanent ENOSYS for the never-implemented set
##           matches upstream exactly; nothing we do can change
##           that without divergence.
##      Limitation: none.  These are the right answers.
##      Bug noted: the find_gaps.py audit script (find_gaps.py at
##      repo root) is now a standing tool — re-run it after any
##      future Linux release to detect new gaps.

##  61. PER-PROCESS CWD (real implementation) — DONE.
##      First "upgrade an existing stub to a real implementation"
##      batch, now that find_gaps.py reports zero undispatched
##      x86_64 syscalls.  Replaces the batch-31 hardcoded "/"
##      response with a real per-process Process::cwd field that
##      chdir updates and getcwd reads.
##         - Process gains `cwd: Vec<u8>` initialized to b"/".
##           fork_create clones the parent's cwd (POSIX rule).
##           pcb::get_cwd / pcb::set_cwd accessors; set_cwd
##           runs invariant checks (starts-with-/, len≤4095,
##           no interior NUL) and rejects with InvalidArgument.
##         - syscall layer adds canonicalize_path(cwd, path)
##           that handles absolute/relative join, multiple //,
##           ./ skip, ../ pop, root-bounded ..  Result is the
##           canonical absolute path with no trailing / except
##           root and length ≤ pcb::CWD_MAX_LEN.
##         - sys_chdir: reads user cstr (PATH_MAX=4096),
##           canonicalizes against cwd, stores via set_cwd.
##         - sys_getcwd: reads pcb::get_cwd(caller_pid),
##           writes path + NUL via copy_to_user.
##         - sys_fchdir: still validate-only success because
##           Linux fd table doesn't yet store path-of-dirfd.
##         - Kernel-context fallback: no caller_pid → still
##           validates and runs canonicalizer, returns 0 on
##           well-formed input, errno on malformed.  Lets the
##           boot self-tests exercise the canonicalizer and
##           error paths in-kernel.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Store the cwd as raw bytes (Vec<u8>), not UTF-8
##           String.  Path bytes are arbitrary on Linux
##           (locale-dependent), and CLAUDE.md mandates
##           OsStr/byte-level handling at the OS boundary.
##         * canonicalize_path is path-string-level only — we
##           don't yet stat the target directory.  Cheaper, and
##           a subsequent open(rel_path) against a nonexistent
##           cwd will fail with ENOENT as it should.  Once the
##           VFS exposes a stat(path) we can add a "verify the
##           target is a directory" check.
##         * Cwd lives on every Process (not just Linux-ABI
##           ones).  Native processes don't expose it via a
##           syscall today but the field is cheap, and the
##           fork-inheritance invariant is simpler when every
##           process has one.
##         * fchdir still stubbed: real implementation needs
##           the linux_fd table to store the original open path
##           alongside (HandleKind, raw_handle).  That is a
##           separate refactor of FdEntry — deferred until a
##           subsequent batch.
##      Limitation: chdir does NOT verify the target exists in
##      the VFS yet.  Programs that chdir to a bogus path see
##      success, then ENOENT on the next open.  Real Linux
##      returns ENOTDIR/ENOENT at the chdir call itself.
##      Limitation: fchdir is still validate-only.  Programs
##      that walk a tree via openat(O_DIRECTORY)+fchdir without
##      re-stringifying paths will silently stay at their
##      original cwd.

##  62. PREAD64 / PWRITE64 / PREADV / PWRITEV / PREADV2 / PWRITEV2
##      real implementations (was ENOSYS) — DONE.
##      Second "upgrade a stub" batch.  Replaces batch-31's "let
##      glibc emulate via lseek+rw+lseek" with real kernel-side
##      positional I/O that preserves the file offset atomically.
##         - fs::handle gains `read_at(handle, offset, &mut buf)`
##           and `write_at(handle, offset, &data)` — pure
##           positional ops that go straight to Vfs::read_at /
##           Vfs::write_at without touching the cached file
##           offset.  POSIX-correct: pwrite ignores O_APPEND.
##         - syscall layer adds `pread_file_to_user` /
##           `pwrite_file_from_user` backends that allocate a
##           kernel buffer, copy_to/from_user, and dispatch to
##           the fs::handle primitives.
##         - sys_pread64 / sys_pwrite64 use them for File
##           handles; Console / Pipe → ESPIPE (POSIX rule:
##           positional I/O on non-seekable fd is ESPIPE, not
##           ENOSYS).
##         - sys_preadv / sys_pwritev / sys_preadv2 / sys_pwritev2
##           walk the iovec array calling the backends with
##           successive offsets.  Linux partial-result semantics
##           preserved: short read mid-iov returns the accumulated
##           total.  preadv2/pwritev2 with offset == -1 delegate
##           to readv/writev (matches Linux: -1 means "use current
##           file offset").
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Adding fs::handle::read_at/write_at as first-class
##           primitives (rather than the seek-save+seek+rw+
##           seek-restore dance glibc would do) gives correct
##           atomicity for free: the file's cached offset
##           literally never changes during a positional op.
##         * ESPIPE (not ENOSYS) for Console/Pipe matches Linux
##           exactly — pread on a pipe is a "wrong tool for the
##           job" error, not a "kernel can't do this" error.
##         * RWF_* flags on preadv2/pwritev2 are accepted (no
##           EOPNOTSUPP except for unknown bits) and treated as
##           hints.  We don't have a block layer that can honour
##           RWF_HIPRI / RWF_DSYNC / RWF_NOWAIT etc., so the hint
##           is silently ignored — same outcome as a Linux kernel
##           on a filesystem that doesn't support the hint.
##         * preadv2(-1) → sys_readv is the cleanest dispatch.
##           pwritev2(-1) → sys_writev, same idea.
##      Limitation: RWF_NOWAIT can't actually trigger EAGAIN for
##      us yet because the VFS is synchronous.  Programs that use
##      it for non-blocking probes will see success rather than
##      EAGAIN — observable, but benign (the read/write itself
##      completes immediately on a synchronous backend).
##      Limitation: short-read accumulation in the iovec walk
##      currently stops at the first short-read.  A more
##      sophisticated impl would keep going across iov entries on
##      "small read", but Linux itself stops at short read on
##      regular files, so this matches.  On pipes Linux behaves
##      differently — but we ESPIPE there anyway.

##  63. GETDENTS64 (real implementation, was ENOSYS) — DONE.
##      Third "upgrade a stub" batch.  Replaces the batch-31
##      ENOSYS placeholder with a real directory iterator backed
##      by fs::handle directory handles + Vfs::readdir_at, so
##      `ls`, glibc readdir(), and any program that needs to
##      enumerate a directory through the Linux ABI now sees real
##      entries instead of "kernel can't list dirs".
##         - fs::handle::OpenFlags gains `DIRECTORY = 1 << 5`.
##         - OpenFile gains `is_directory: bool`.  Directory
##           handles reuse the `offset` field as an entry cursor
##           (entry index into the VFS listing).
##         - fs::handle::open() now honours DIRECTORY:
##             dir + DIRECTORY     → allocate_dir_handle
##             dir + no DIRECTORY  → IsADirectory (existing)
##             file + DIRECTORY    → NotADirectory
##             file + no DIRECTORY → existing
##           DIRECTORY combined with TRUNCATE/CREATE/APPEND/
##           WRITE is rejected with IsADirectory (matches Linux
##           rejecting nonsensical combos rather than silently
##           ignoring flags).  O_DIRECTORY|O_CREAT on a missing
##           path returns ENOENT (mkdir is the way to create
##           directories, not open).
##         - Byte-oriented ops on a dir handle (read / write /
##           seek / read_at / write_at / ftruncate) all fail with
##           IsADirectory.
##         - New `read_dir_at(handle, max)` returns
##           (start_cursor, Vec<DirEntry>) without advancing the
##           cursor.  New `set_dir_cursor(handle, cursor)`
##           advances/rewinds.  Split is deliberate: getdents64
##           may consume only a prefix of a page when the user
##           buffer fills, and must then commit exactly the
##           consumed count back as the new cursor.
##         - dup() preserves is_directory and the cursor across
##           the duplicate.
##         - syscall layer: translate_open_flags maps
##           O_DIRECTORY → OpenFlags::DIRECTORY so plain Linux
##           open(O_RDONLY|O_DIRECTORY) now returns a proper dir
##           fd that getdents64 can consume.
##         - sys_getdents64 implementation:
##             * Validate fd, count, user buffer.
##             * lookup_caller_fd → must be HandleKind::File
##               (dir handles are file-kind underneath).
##             * read_dir_at(handle, 256) for a page.
##             * Encode each entry as `struct linux_dirent64`:
##               u64 d_ino + s64 d_off + u16 d_reclen + u8 d_type
##               + NUL-terminated name, padded to 8-byte align.
##             * d_ino synthesized via FNV-1a hash over
##               dir_path + "/" + name (forced non-zero).
##             * d_type maps EntryType → DT_REG/DT_DIR/DT_LNK/
##               DT_UNKNOWN.
##             * Stops when the next record won't fit; advances
##               cursor by entries actually consumed.
##             * Return values match Linux: >0 bytes written,
##               0 at EOD, EINVAL if buf can't hold first entry,
##               ENOTDIR for file-fd, EBADF for unknown fd.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Reuse fs::handle's offset field as the cursor
##           rather than adding a separate dir_cursor field.
##           OpenFile is already two words (offset+size) of
##           position state; teaching it about "this u64 means
##           entry index when is_directory" is cheaper than
##           growing the struct and keeps dup/dup_shared trivial.
##         * Synthesizing d_ino from a hash of path+name rather
##           than threading inode numbers up from the FS layer.
##           POSIX explicitly allows readdir to return any
##           non-zero value for d_ino if the FS doesn't expose
##           stable inodes (FAT is the canonical example), and
##           our ext4 port hasn't propagated real inodes yet.
##           When it does, the hash falls away.
##         * d_off = cursor_after_entry rather than entry_index.
##           That way `lseek(dirfd, d_off, SEEK_SET)` can resume
##           iteration at the right place if/when we wire dir
##           seek (currently dir-handle seek is IsADirectory; a
##           future patch will make Start(cursor) work).
##         * Encoding entirely in a kernel-side scratch buffer
##           and copy_to_user only once at the end keeps the
##           SMAP window tight and avoids partial writes that
##           a SIGSEGV mid-encode would otherwise leave behind.
##         * Filter out entries whose name contains '/' or NUL
##           defensively.  Our VFS already rejects them at
##           ingest, but a corrupted on-disk FS could surface
##           them and would corrupt the userspace parser if we
##           passed them through.  Skip-and-advance is the right
##           call: don't drop the iteration just because one
##           entry is malformed.
##      Limitation: d_ino is not stable across kernel boots
##      (depends on the canonical path string).  Programs that
##      cache inode numbers across reboots to detect "same file"
##      will lose that.  Fixes itself once the FS exposes real
##      inodes.
##      Limitation: dir handle seek (lseek on a dir fd) still
##      returns IsADirectory.  glibc rewinddir uses lseek(0)
##      under the hood and currently fails — programs should use
##      a fresh openat instead until we add the seek path.  d_off
##      values are already cursor-compatible so the patch is
##      mechanical when it lands.
##      Limitation: getdents (legacy 32-bit dirent) is still
##      ENOSYS.  glibc has used getdents64 exclusively since 2.x,
##      so this only affects static binaries from the early-2000s
##      era and the upgrade isn't worth the layout duplication.

##  64. FLOCK (real Vfs::flock backend, was no-op) — DONE.
##      Fourth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Replaces the previous
##      "always succeed regardless of contention" behaviour with
##      a real call into the Vfs lock table, so two processes
##      that flock the same path actually see the conflict.
##         - sys_flock now does fd→handle→path lookup via
##           lookup_caller_fd + fs::handle::handle_path.
##         - Console/Pipe fds → EBADF (no backing path).
##         - Unknown op bits → EINVAL (matches Linux's "kernel
##           refuses request it doesn't understand").
##         - SH|EX combined → EINVAL.
##         - LOCK_SH → Vfs::flock(path, handle_id, Shared).
##         - LOCK_EX → Vfs::flock(path, handle_id, Exclusive).
##         - LOCK_UN → Vfs::funlock(path, handle_id).
##         - VFS WouldBlock → EAGAIN (== EWOULDBLOCK on Linux).
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Using the kernel handle id as the owner makes
##           auto-release on close cost-free — fs::handle::close
##           already invokes funlock(path, handle_id) when the
##           final reference drops, so the lock dies with the
##           description.  Forked children inheriting the
##           description (dup_shared semantics) share the same
##           owner id and thus the same lock, matching Linux's
##           open-file-description semantics for flock.
##         * EBADF for Console/Pipe rather than ENOTSUP because
##           glibc / userspace probes treat "this fd has no
##           lockable backing" identically to "bad fd" — both
##           cause the caller to fall back to no locking — and
##           EBADF is the conventional answer for flock-on-pty.
##         * VFS already supports upgrade/downgrade and "owner
##           already holds" — we just thread the call through.
##           No new lock-table code needed for batch 38.
##      Boot self-test exercises:
##         - kernel-context unknown fd → EBADF for SH / EX /
##           UN (validates the lookup_caller_fd path).
##         - Bad op bits → EINVAL.
##         - SH|EX combined → EINVAL.
##         - End-to-end via Vfs::flock on a real handle:
##             acquire EX, conflict with different owner →
##             WouldBlock, release-on-close → lock_query None.
##      Limitation: LOCK_NB (without it) is supposed to BLOCK on
##      contention.  We don't yet have a wait queue hook in the
##      VFS lock table, so we return EAGAIN regardless of LOCK_NB.
##      Editors / lockfile probes that already pass LOCK_NB get
##      the right answer; programs that rely on blocking flock
##      see an early failure and must retry.  Fix path: add
##      a wait_list: Vec<TaskId> to PathLockEntry, park the
##      caller via proc::wait_queue when contended, and wake on
##      funlock.  Tracked here for a follow-up batch.
##      Limitation: Vfs::flock is whole-file only; flock(2) is
##      whole-file by definition, so this is correct.  POSIX
##      fcntl(F_SETLK) byte-range locking is a separate path
##      (sys_fcntl currently stubs F_SETLK as 0) and would need
##      a range-locking table; tracked separately.

##  65. CHDIR target verification + real FCHDIR — DONE.
##      Fifth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Closes two documented
##      batch-35 limitations: chdir didn't verify the target
##      existed (lazy ENOENT on next open) and fchdir was a
##      validate-only no-op.
##         - sys_chdir: after canonicalize_path produces a
##           candidate cwd, stat it via Vfs::stat.  NotFound →
##           ENOENT, exists-but-not-dir → ENOTDIR, otherwise
##           commit via pcb::set_cwd.  Matches Linux's "the
##           error fires at chdir, not at the next file op".
##           Kernel-context branch unchanged (still validate-
##           only, used by self-tests).
##         - sys_fchdir: real implementation.  lookup_caller_fd
##           → must be HandleKind::File → fs::handle::handle_path
##           recovers the original open path → re-stat to confirm
##           it's still a directory → pcb::set_cwd.  No FdEntry
##           refactor required: the path the fd was opened with
##           already lives in the fs::handle OpenFile entry, so
##           we just borrow what handle.rs already remembers.
##           Console/Pipe fds → ENOTDIR (rather than EBADF —
##           Linux returns ENOTDIR for fchdir-on-pipe).
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Re-statting at fchdir rather than caching is-a-dir
##           on the FdEntry catches the rmdir-while-open race
##           naturally — programs see ENOENT just like Linux's
##           fchdir would.
##         * Recovering the path from fs::handle (rather than
##           growing FdEntry with a String path field) keeps
##           KernelFdTable a fixed-size [Option<FdEntry>; MAX_FDS]
##           array of Copy entries.  The path lives in exactly
##           one place (OpenFile) and is reachable from anywhere
##           we hold a raw_handle.  Same trick will work for
##           openat(dirfd, ...) when we wire that up.
##         * In sys_chdir, doing the stat after canonicalize_path
##           (rather than inside) keeps the canonicalizer a pure
##           string transform — easier to unit-test in isolation
##           via the boot self-test's 14-case table.
##      Limitation: openat with a non-AT_FDCWD dirfd still
##      doesn't honour the dirfd as a starting directory for
##      relative paths.  Same path-from-handle recovery applies;
##      tracked as a separate batch.
##      Limitation: a chdir target that exists at chdir time but
##      is removed before the next openat will still see ENOENT
##      at the openat (no caching).  This matches Linux exactly.

##  66. OPENAT dirfd resolution — DONE.
##      Sixth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Closes the limitation
##      flagged in item 65: openat(non-AT_FDCWD, relative_path)
##      now honours the dirfd as the resolution root rather than
##      silently falling through to AT_FDCWD.
##         - sys_openat: branch on the first path byte.  AT_FDCWD
##           → open_common (existing behaviour).  Absolute path
##           (first byte '/') → open_common (POSIX: dirfd is
##           ignored for absolute paths).  Empty path → ENOENT
##           (no AT_EMPTY_PATH support yet — openat2 territory).
##           Otherwise: lookup_caller_fd(dirfd), require
##           HandleKind::File, recover the directory path via
##           fs::handle::handle_path, stat-verify it's still a
##           directory (ENOTDIR for regular files, ENOENT for
##           rmdir-while-open races), concatenate dir_path + "/"
##           + rel_bytes, ENAMETOOLONG on >4095 bytes, then route
##           through the new open_kernel_path_install helper.
##         - open_kernel_path_install(path, flags): new helper
##           that bypasses the user-pointer copy stage of
##           open_common.  Does cap check → translate_open_flags
##           → fs::handle::open(path) → register_ipc_handle →
##           build FdEntry with FD_CLOEXEC + status flags →
##           pcb::linux_fd_install.  Rolls back both the IPC
##           handle registration and the underlying file open on
##           any install failure so we never leak the raw handle.
##         - handlers::require_cap_type made pub(crate) so
##           linux.rs can reuse the existing cap-check helper
##           without duplicating the pid/kernel-bypass logic.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * The path lives in exactly one place (fs::handle
##           OpenFile).  Borrowing it via handle_path keeps
##           FdEntry a fixed-size Copy struct — no String fields
##           bloating the [Option<FdEntry>; MAX_FDS] table.
##         * Stat-verifying the dirfd at openat (rather than
##           caching is-a-dir on FdEntry) catches the
##           rmdir-while-fd-open race naturally.  Programs see
##           ENOENT, matching Linux exactly.
##         * Peeking only the first byte of the user path before
##           the dirfd lookup keeps absolute-path opens cheap —
##           we don't waste the lookup on requests that ignore
##           dirfd anyway.
##         * Empty path → ENOENT, not AT_EMPTY_PATH.  Honouring
##           AT_EMPTY_PATH requires the openat2 flags path, which
##           we deliberately ENOSYS today (callers fall back to
##           openat).  Tracked separately.
##      Limitation: O_NOFOLLOW on the dirfd is not enforced — if
##      the dirfd was opened with O_NOFOLLOW but its underlying
##      path contains symlinks elsewhere, the relative open will
##      still resolve through them.  Symlink-safe resolution
##      requires a dcache-walking primitive that we don't have
##      yet.
##      Limitation: AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW / AT_EMPTY_PATH flags
##      (passed via openat's mode argument in openat2) are not
##      honoured — sys_openat only consumes the dirfd, path, and
##      flags args.  Add when openat2 grows beyond ENOSYS.
##      Limitation: We re-stat the dirfd's backing path at every
##      openat call rather than caching directoriness in the
##      FdEntry.  Correct under the rmdir-while-open race, but
##      slower than Linux's dcache.  Acceptable until benchmarks
##      flag it.

##  67. Per-process rlimit storage — DONE.
##      Seventh "upgrade a stub" batch.  Closes the limitation
##      flagged in item 11 (prlimit was validate-then-discard).
##      Programs that lower then re-read their resource limits
##      (a common sandbox-setup idiom in shells, languages, and
##      service supervisors) now see consistent state.
##         - kernel/src/proc/pcb.rs: added
##           `pub rlimits: [(u64, u64); 16]` to Process; const
##           `DEFAULT_RLIMITS: [(u64, u64); 16]` initialised on
##           every Process::new(); `RLIM_INFINITY = u64::MAX`
##           and `NUM_RLIMITS = 16` constants.
##         - fork_create clones the parent's rlimits (POSIX
##           inheritance — independent thereafter).
##         - pcb::get_rlimit(pid, resource) and
##           pcb::set_rlimit(pid, resource, cur, max) — the
##           latter enforces cur ≤ max (InvalidArgument) and
##           new.max ≤ old.max (PermissionDenied, no
##           CAP_SYS_RESOURCE equivalent yet).
##         - sys_prlimit64 in linux.rs rewritten: reads existing
##           via pcb::get_rlimit, installs new via pcb::set_rlimit,
##           writes the pre-install snapshot to old_limit_ptr
##           (matching Linux's atomic read-then-write semantics).
##           Kernel-context callers fall back to DEFAULT_RLIMITS
##           — boot self-tests still validate-only.
##         - sys_getrlimit and sys_setrlimit unchanged: they
##           already forward to sys_prlimit64 with pid=0, so
##           they automatically gain the per-process backing.
##         - Removed the now-redundant `rlimit_default` helper
##           from linux.rs; replaced its self-test by indexing
##           `pcb::DEFAULT_RLIMITS` directly.
##      New direct-API self-test block exercises:
##         - DEFAULT_RLIMITS for fresh processes.
##         - set_rlimit lowers cur+max together.
##         - Raising max -> PermissionDenied.
##         - cur > max -> InvalidArgument.
##         - resource >= NUM_RLIMITS -> InvalidArgument
##           (set) / None (get).
##         - Cleanup via pcb::destroy so the throwaway PID isn't
##           leaked into the table.
##      New syscall-level self-tests:
##         - prlimit64 read STACK old_limit -> DEFAULT_RLIMITS[3].
##         - prlimit64 new(cur > max) -> EINVAL.
##         - prlimit64 set NOFILE in kernel ctx -> 0 (validate-
##           only) and old_limit -> DEFAULT_RLIMITS[7].
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Fixed-size [(u64, u64); 16] array on the Process is
##           the smallest data structure that holds the full Linux
##           rlimit space.  At 256 bytes per process the cost is
##           trivial vs Vec/HashMap alternatives, and indexing is
##           O(1) without allocator pressure on the resize-down
##           setrlimit path.
##         * Defaults live in pcb.rs (not linux.rs) so they're
##           available to Process::new() without a cross-crate
##           call.  The syscall layer (linux.rs) reads them via
##           pcb::DEFAULT_RLIMITS rather than duplicating.
##         * Enforcing cur ≤ max in pcb::set_rlimit (not just at
##           the syscall layer) means any future internal caller
##           (a future cgroup-style resource controller, say) is
##           forced into the same invariant.
##         * Hard-limit raise -> PermissionDenied rather than
##           silently accepted: we don't have CAP_SYS_RESOURCE
##           machinery yet, so the only correct answer is "no".
##           Programs that need to raise have to wait for the
##           privilege model to land.
##      Limitation: Most of these limits are not actually
##      enforced.  RLIMIT_NOFILE doesn't gate fd allocation;
##      RLIMIT_STACK doesn't gate stack growth; RLIMIT_AS
##      doesn't gate mmap.  Storage now exists, so enforcement
##      can be wired up subsystem-by-subsystem as a follow-up.
##      Listed in priority order:
##         * RLIMIT_NOFILE   — enforce in pcb::linux_fd_install.
##         * RLIMIT_AS       — enforce in sys_mmap / brk.
##         * RLIMIT_STACK    — enforce in stack-growth path.
##         * RLIMIT_NPROC    — enforce in pcb::create / fork.
##         * RLIMIT_FSIZE    — enforce in write paths.
##         * RLIMIT_CPU      — needs a CPU accounting subsystem.
##      Limitation: No CAP_SYS_RESOURCE equivalent.  Hard-limit
##      raises always fail.  Add when the cap-name table grows
##      beyond the current set.
##      Limitation: Cross-process prlimit (pid != self) still
##      returns EPERM unconditionally.  Linux allows it with
##      CAP_SYS_RESOURCE or when the caller's uid matches the
##      target's uid + ruid.  Same caveat as the privilege
##      limitation above — comes with the cap model.

##  68. Enforce RLIMIT_NOFILE in linux_fd_install — DONE.
##      Eighth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Wires the rlimit store
##      added in item 67 into the central Linux fd install
##      choke point so the first storage→enforcement link in
##      the enforcement-priority list takes effect.
##         - pcb::linux_fd_install: after install_lowest_from
##           returns the chosen fd, compare against the
##           process's RLIMIT_NOFILE soft limit
##           (`proc.rlimits[7].0`).  If `fd >= soft`, roll the
##           install back via fd_table.take(fd) and surface
##           TooManyOpenFiles (which the syscall layer already
##           translates to EMFILE).  RLIM_INFINITY skips the
##           check entirely.
##         - Snapshot the soft limit before borrowing the fd
##           table mutably (avoids a double-borrow on `proc`).
##      Coverage in the rlimit self-test block:
##         - Stdio (fds 0,1,2) + soft=5 → fds 3 and 4 install
##           cleanly, fd 5 → TooManyOpenFiles.
##         - Raising soft to 100 and re-installing must yield
##           fd 5 (proves the failed install rolled back; no
##           leaked entry left behind).
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Enforcing in linux_fd_install (PCB layer) catches
##           every install path uniformly — open_common, the
##           batch 40 open_kernel_path_install helper, pipe,
##           pipe2, dup, dup2, dup3, fcntl(F_DUPFD),
##           socketpair, accept, accept4, eventfd, signalfd,
##           timerfd, and every future install caller.
##           Enforcing in the syscall layer would require
##           duplicate checks at each call site.
##         * Rolling back via fd_table.take(fd) on EMFILE
##           keeps the table consistent.  Without rollback, a
##           failed install would leak the entry into the
##           table — installable but un-closable since the
##           caller never saw the fd.
##         * Snapshotting nofile_soft before the mutable
##           borrow on fd_table sidesteps Rust's borrow rules
##           cleanly: a single shared lock on PROCESS_TABLE,
##           one read then one write on the same `proc`
##           reference.
##         * `RLIM_INFINITY` skip rather than `u64::MAX as i32`
##           comparison: the sentinel is the documented value;
##           comparing fd (i32, max ~2 billion) against an
##           infinity u64 is well-defined and cheap.
##      Limitation: ENFILE (system-wide fd exhaustion) is not
##      tracked separately.  We have no global open-file
##      counter; processes always see EMFILE first.  Adding a
##      global counter would be straightforward (atomic
##      counter incremented in install, decremented in close)
##      but premature without a published system-wide cap.
##      Limitation: The check happens *after* allocation, not
##      before.  install_lowest_from scans for the lowest free
##      slot and returns its index; if that index ≥ soft, we
##      roll back.  This is correct but slightly wasteful when
##      the soft limit is very low — we scan further than
##      strictly necessary.  Acceptable until profiling flags
##      it.

##  69. Enforce RLIMIT_NPROC in fork_create — DONE.
##      Ninth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Adds the second
##      storage→enforcement link from item 67's priority list.
##      Userspace fork now sees EAGAIN when the parent's uid
##      already owns rlim_cur(NPROC) processes.
##         - pcb::fork_create: after snapshotting the parent's
##           rlimits + credentials, walk PROCESS_TABLE counting
##           processes whose credentials.uid matches.  If
##           (count + 1) > rlimits[6].0 → return WouldBlock
##           (mapped to EAGAIN at the syscall layer).
##         - uid 0 is exempt by convention (Linux uses
##           CAP_SYS_RESOURCE / CAP_SYS_ADMIN; we have no cap
##           model wired up, so root is treated as exempt —
##           same effective behaviour for the systems we run).
##         - RLIM_INFINITY skips the check entirely.
##         - pcb::create (kernel-spawned processes like init)
##           is intentionally NOT gated — RLIMIT_NPROC is a
##           userspace-fork-only limit on Linux too.
##      Coverage in the rlimit self-test block:
##         - Parent with uid=1000 + NPROC.cur=1 → fork
##           rejected with WouldBlock (1 existing + 1 new = 2
##           > 1).
##         - Raise NPROC.cur to 2 → one fork succeeds.
##         - Another fork → WouldBlock (count + 1 = 3 > 2).
##         - Parent with uid=0 + NPROC.cur=0 → fork still
##           succeeds (root exemption).
##         - Clean up all throwaway pids via pcb::destroy.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Enforcing in fork_create catches every userspace
##           process-creation path that flows through the PCB
##           layer.  pcb::create (kernel-spawned) deliberately
##           skips the check so service-manager bootstrap and
##           init can't be locked out.
##         * Counting includes zombies (per Linux): a zombie
##           still holds the uid quota until reaped.  The walk
##           doesn't filter on ProcessState, which is correct.
##         * Rejecting before alloc_pid keeps the PID pool clean
##           on the failure path — no leaked PIDs.
##         * Holding the PROCESS_TABLE lock across the count
##           and the insert keeps the check atomic with respect
##           to other forks.  Without this, two concurrent
##           forks could each see "room for one more" and both
##           install, blowing past the limit.
##      Limitation: We exempt uid=0 instead of CAP_SYS_RESOURCE
##      because we don't have a real capability check for that
##      cap.  When the cap model lands, swap the uid check for
##      `has_capability(CAP_SYS_RESOURCE)`.
##      Limitation: The per-uid count is O(N_processes).  Fine
##      for the dozens-to-hundreds of processes a desktop runs;
##      a per-uid counter cache would be needed for thousands.
##      Acceptable until profiling flags it.
##      Limitation: Threads (created via clone with CLONE_THREAD)
##      are not currently distinguished from processes here.
##      They're tracked separately via the thread table, so they
##      don't show up in PROCESS_TABLE and don't count against
##      NPROC.  Matches Linux's actual semantics (NPROC counts
##      *processes*, not threads), but worth noting because some
##      kernels conflate the two.

##  70. Enforce RLIMIT_AS in Linux sys_mmap / sys_munmap — DONE.
##      Tenth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Third storage→enforcement
##      link from item 67's priority list.  Userspace `mmap(2)`
##      now sees ENOMEM when the new mapping would push the
##      process past `rlim_cur(RLIMIT_AS)`.
##         - pcb::linux_as_bytes field added to Process, init=0,
##           inherited verbatim across fork_create (the child's
##           CoW address space mirrors the parent's).
##         - pcb::linux_as_charge(pid, bytes) checks soft limit
##           and bumps the counter atomically under PROCESS_TABLE
##           lock; returns OutOfMemory (→ ENOMEM at the syscall
##           boundary) if exceeding.
##         - pcb::linux_as_release(pid, bytes) decrements with
##           saturating_sub so an over-release clamps to zero
##           instead of wrapping.
##         - pcb::linux_as_used(pid) reads the counter for self-
##           tests and future /proc/<pid>/statm.
##         - pcb::RLIMIT_AS_INDEX = 9 named constant so call sites
##           don't repeat the magic number.
##         - linux::sys_mmap: round length up to FRAME_SIZE,
##           charge before delegating to handlers::sys_mmap, and
##           release on native-mmap failure (so a partial failure
##           doesn't leak accounting space).
##         - linux::sys_munmap: on successful native unmap,
##           release the same aligned length.  Failed munmaps
##           don't refund (no pages actually taken back).
##         - Kernel-context callers (caller_pid() == None) skip
##           accounting entirely — a per-process limit doesn't
##           apply to processes that don't exist.
##      Coverage in the rlimit self-test block:
##         - Fresh PID starts at 0 bytes.
##         - Set AS soft = 64 KiB; charge exactly 64 KiB → ok.
##         - +1 byte over → OutOfMemory; counter unchanged (the
##           failed charge must not bump linux_as_bytes).
##         - Release half; recharge half → ok and back to limit.
##         - Saturating release: release u64::MAX clamps to 0.
##         - RLIM_INFINITY soft accepts u64::MAX/2 charge.
##         - fork_create: child inherits parent's
##           linux_as_bytes; subsequent release on child does
##           not affect parent (independent accounting after
##           fork).
##         - Clean up throwaway pids via pcb::destroy.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * RLIMIT_AS is a Linux-ABI concept; only the Linux
##           translation layer charges/releases.  Native programs
##           are unaffected — matches the design (native syscalls
##           pre-date the Linux ABI and have their own model).
##         * Charging the aligned length (not raw length) matches
##           what the kernel actually allocates and what
##           /proc/<pid>/maps would show.
##         * Charging at sys_mmap entry (after argument validation
##           but before delegating to native) keeps the failure
##           path simple: on native failure we refund; on success
##           the charge already stuck.
##         * Fork inherits the charge so the child sees the same
##           accounting view as if it had just executed all the
##           parent's mmaps itself.  This matches what /proc would
##           report on Linux after a fork.
##      Limitation: We don't track per-mapping charges, so a
##      munmap with a size larger than the original mmap will
##      under-account (saturating_sub clamps at 0).  Programs
##      that munmap exact-size or smaller see correct numbers.
##      Acceptable until a real VMA splitter/merger lands.
##      Limitation: brk(2) doesn't yet charge — sys_brk is still
##      a "claim the heap is whatever you asked for" stub.  When
##      we wire a real brk-region VMA, it should charge AS too.
##      Limitation: Stack growth (lazy stack fault path) doesn't
##      charge.  When RLIMIT_STACK lands as its own enforcement
##      batch, that path should both check STACK and charge AS.
##      Limitation: File-backed and shared-anon mmap return
##      ENOSYS today, so AS only meaningfully counts private
##      anonymous mappings.  Will need updating when those land.

##  71. Enforce RLIMIT_FSIZE in pwrite / pwritev / pwritev2 /
##      ftruncate / truncate — DONE.
##      Eleventh "upgrade a stub" batch.  Fourth storage→
##      enforcement link from item 67's priority list.
##      Positional writes and explicit truncates now honour
##      `rlim_cur(RLIMIT_FSIZE)`, returning EFBIG (or clipping
##      to a partial write) per Linux semantics.
##         - pcb::RLIMIT_FSIZE_INDEX = 1 named constant added.
##         - linux::rlimit_fsize_clip_with(soft, offset, len):
##           pure decision routine.  RLIM_INFINITY -> Ok(len);
##           offset >= soft -> Err(EFBIG); otherwise
##           Ok(min(len, soft - offset)).
##         - linux::rlimit_fsize_clip_for_caller(offset, len):
##           thin wrapper that fetches the caller's pid +
##           rlim_cur(RLIMIT_FSIZE) and delegates to _with.
##           Kernel-context callers (pid == None) pass through
##           unchecked.
##         - linux::rlimit_fsize_check_size_with(soft, new_size)
##           and ..._for_caller(new_size): exact-size variant
##           for truncate paths.  new_size > soft -> Err(EFBIG)
##           (equal allowed, unlike pwrite where offset == soft
##           is EFBIG).
##         - Wired into pwrite_file_from_user so all positional
##           write paths (pwrite64, pwritev, pwritev2) clip
##           uniformly.
##         - sys_ftruncate and sys_truncate now check size
##           before falling through to EROFS — Linux ordering
##           (limit fires before the FS error).
##      Coverage in the rlimit self-test block:
##         - RLIM_INFINITY soft: pass-through clip / check at
##           u64::MAX boundary.
##         - Finite soft=1024: exact-fit, mid-file fit,
##           straddling clip to soft - offset, oversized clip,
##           offset==soft EFBIG, offset>soft EFBIG, MAX-offset
##           EFBIG without overflow.
##         - Zero-length write returns 0 even at boundary.
##         - soft=0 rejects any non-zero write.
##         - Truncate: size==soft allowed, size>soft EFBIG,
##           size>0 with soft=0 EFBIG.
##         - Kernel-context callers always pass through.
##         - Dispatch-level: sys_ftruncate without a pid still
##           returns EROFS via the no-pid fallthrough.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Plugging the check into pwrite_file_from_user
##           catches every positional write path through one
##           gateway (DRY).  The non-positional write paths
##           (write/writev) need the file's current offset,
##           which requires a new fs::handle accessor — left
##           to a follow-up batch since pwrite/pwritev/pwritev2
##           cover the explicit-offset cases that matter for
##           limit-aware programs.
##         * Truncate uses a separate "exact size" check (not
##           the clip variant) because the new file size is
##           the argument, not bytes added to a current size.
##         * Limit check fires *before* the EROFS / EBADF
##           checks where possible, matching Linux's ordering
##           and giving consistent EFBIG to programs that lower
##           RLIMIT_FSIZE regardless of FS state.
##         * Pure-helper / _for_caller split makes the
##           self-tests deterministic — we exercise the
##           decision table without needing to inject a fake
##           caller_pid().
##      Limitation: write/writev/writev2 (current-offset
##      variants) are NOT yet clipped.  They need an fs::handle
##      accessor that returns the effective next write offset
##      (current pos, or size for O_APPEND).  Adding that
##      accessor + clip is the natural next batch.
##      Limitation: SIGXFSZ delivery is not yet implemented.
##      Linux delivers SIGXFSZ alongside the EFBIG return so
##      programs can install a handler to react to limit
##      breaches.  Our EFBIG is correct; the signal will land
##      when signal-delivery is finished.
##      Limitation: ftruncate and truncate both still return
##      EROFS after the RLIMIT_FSIZE check passes — the actual
##      truncate path doesn't yet exist.  The new check is a
##      no-op visibly for programs that don't lower
##      RLIMIT_FSIZE, but it gives correct behaviour for
##      programs that DO lower it (they see EFBIG instead of
##      EROFS, matching what Linux would report).

##  72. Extend RLIMIT_FSIZE enforcement to write / writev
##      (current-offset write paths) — DONE.
##      Twelfth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Closes the limitation
##      noted in item 71: the non-positional write syscalls now
##      participate in the same RLIMIT_FSIZE clipping that
##      pwrite/pwritev already use.
##         - fs::handle::peek_write_offset(handle) ->
##           KernelResult<u64> added.  Returns file.size for
##           handles with OpenFlags::APPEND set (POSIX rule:
##           append writes go to EOF) and file.offset
##           otherwise.  Validates the same conditions as
##           write: writable flag, not a directory.  Used
##           exclusively by the Linux ABI today; the native
##           write paths don't have a notion of RLIMIT_FSIZE
##           and don't call it.
##         - linux::dispatch_write, in the HandleKind::File
##           arm, now calls peek_write_offset → clip via
##           rlimit_fsize_clip_for_caller → pass the (possibly
##           reduced) len to handlers::sys_fs_write.  EFBIG
##           short-circuits the dispatch.  peek_write_offset
##           errors (InvalidHandle, IsADirectory,
##           PermissionDenied) fall through with the original
##           len so the user sees the same errno they would
##           have seen without the rlimit check.
##      Coverage:
##         - Pure decision-table tests already exercise the
##           clip math (item 71).
##         - peek_write_offset(0) and peek_write_offset(MAX)
##           both return InvalidHandle, confirming the new
##           accessor is wired up and reachable from the
##           rlimit self-test block.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * A peek + write pair has a TOCTOU window if two
##           holders of the same fd write concurrently.  Linux
##           has the identical race in its VFS write path,
##           because RLIMIT_FSIZE is a policy guard not a
##           security boundary.  Acceptable.
##         * peek_write_offset is a fs::handle responsibility
##           even though it exists solely for the Linux ABI —
##           the function reaches into private fields (offset,
##           size, flags) that are only visible inside the
##           module, so making the dispatcher do it would
##           require exposing those internals.
##         * Falling through on peek errors (rather than
##           propagating them) keeps the user-visible errno
##           identical to the pre-rlimit dispatch for non-write
##           handle states.  The actual write attempt will
##           rediscover the same condition via sys_fs_write.
##      Limitation: SIGXFSZ still not delivered (same as item
##      71).  EFBIG is correct; signal delivery is a separate
##      batch when signals lands.
##      Limitation: write/writev paths through HandleKind::Pipe
##      and HandleKind::Console are not clipped — pipes and
##      consoles are not regular files and don't accumulate
##      bytes against RLIMIT_FSIZE.  Matches Linux semantics.
##      Limitation: The non-Linux native sys_fs_write path
##      bypasses the clip entirely.  Native programs aren't
##      subject to RLIMIT_FSIZE in our model, which matches
##      the parallel treatment of RLIMIT_AS in batch 44.

##  73. Enforce RLIMIT_STACK in idt::try_grow_user_stack — DONE.
##      Thirteenth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Bounds on-demand
##      user stack growth by the per-process Linux RLIMIT_STACK
##      soft limit, in addition to the existing compile-time
##      USER_STACK_GUARD and runtime sysctl mm.max_stack_frames
##      guards.  The effective stack floor is now the
##      maximum (i.e. most restrictive) of all three terms.
##         - pcb::RLIMIT_STACK_INDEX = 3 named constant added
##           so the page fault handler doesn't repeat the magic
##           number.
##         - pcb::try_get_rlimit(pid, resource) added.  Uses
##           PROCESS_TABLE.try_lock() and returns None on lock
##           contention, on unknown pid, or on out-of-range
##           resource.  This is the only safe accessor for
##           interrupt context — the regular get_rlimit() would
##           deadlock if a syscall holding the table happened
##           to fault its own stack.
##         - idt::try_grow_user_stack(cr2, error, pid) gained
##           a pid parameter (the caller already had pid for
##           the try_resolve_fault step).  When pid != 0 it
##           consults try_get_rlimit(STACK); a finite soft
##           limit yields rlimit_guard = USER_STACK_TOP -
##           soft_bytes, and effective_guard is the max of
##           USER_STACK_GUARD, dynamic_guard (sysctl), and
##           rlimit_guard.  RLIM_INFINITY and None (contention
##           or unknown pid) both fall back to USER_STACK_GUARD,
##           contributing nothing to the bound.
##      Coverage:
##         - try_get_rlimit returns DEFAULT_RLIMITS[3] = (8 MiB,
##           RLIM_INFINITY) for a freshly-created pid.
##         - After set_rlimit(pid, 3, 64 KiB, 64 KiB),
##           try_get_rlimit observes the lowered value.
##         - try_get_rlimit on an unknown pid -> None.
##         - try_get_rlimit with resource = NUM_RLIMITS -> None
##           (out-of-range rejection preserved).
##         - Cross-resource sanity: try_get_rlimit(AS) returns
##           the default (RLIM_INFINITY, RLIM_INFINITY), proving
##           the same accessor serves every resource index.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * try_lock with fall-through-on-contention is the
##           conservative correct path for a #PF handler: worst
##           case is "same as before this batch" (no rlimit
##           term applied), best case is the limit is honored.
##           Blocking on the lock would risk deadlock against
##           any syscall that holds PROCESS_TABLE and faults its
##           own stack while doing so.
##         * Threading pid through as a third arg rather than
##           re-looking-it-up inside try_grow_user_stack avoids
##           a redundant sched::current_task_id() →
##           thread::owner_process() pair on every #PF, and
##           lets the existing pid == 0 (kernel/early-boot)
##           check in the caller continue to gate the rlimit
##           lookup.
##         * Using saturating_sub keeps the math safe for soft
##           limits larger than USER_STACK_TOP — they pin
##           rlimit_guard to 0, which is never selected because
##           USER_STACK_GUARD is always larger.
##      Limitation: getrlimit(RLIMIT_STACK) still reports the
##      pcb value, not the dynamic sysctl-derived limit.  glibc
##      uses the rlimit for thread stack sizing; that's fine
##      because the sysctl is meant to be a per-system cap and
##      should be set high enough to accommodate the rlimit.
##      If sysctl is *lower* than rlimit, the page fault handler
##      will refuse to grow past the sysctl bound — that's the
##      same behavior we had before this batch, and matches the
##      Linux semantics of the sysctl as an administrative cap.
##      Limitation: setrlimit(RLIMIT_STACK) doesn't shrink an
##      already-grown stack.  Linux has the same behavior:
##      lowering the limit only affects future growth, not
##      pages that are already mapped.
##      Limitation: RLIMIT_STACK does not yet trigger SIGSEGV
##      on overflow with a meaningful si_code distinguishing
##      stack-overflow from generic access-violation — the page
##      fault handler falls through to the standard SEH /
##      AccessViolation path when growth is refused.  Once
##      Linux signal delivery lands, the si_code should be set
##      to SEGV_BNDERR or similar for stack-overflow refusals.

##  74. Fix getpriority return value + enforce RLIMIT_NICE
##      in setpriority — DONE.
##      Fourteenth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Two parallel fixes
##      under the Linux scheduler-stub umbrella:
##         a) sys_getpriority: returns 20 (= 20 - nice with
##            nice=0), matching Linux's kernel-ABI return
##            convention.  Previously returned 0, which glibc's
##            wrapper would have translated to nice=20 (the
##            lowest priority).  Programs that called
##            getpriority(2) directly and trusted the return
##            value would have been told they were at the very
##            bottom of the priority order — wrong.
##         b) sys_setpriority: enforces RLIMIT_NICE via a new
##            rlimit_nice_check_for_caller / _with helper pair.
##            Linux semantics: a priority boost (new_nice < 0)
##            requires either CAP_SYS_NICE or new_nice >=
##            (20 - rlim_cur(RLIMIT_NICE)).  We have no
##            CAP_SYS_NICE, so the rlimit is the only gate.
##            DEFAULT_RLIMITS[13] = (0, 0) means a default
##            process has floor=20 and cannot boost at all,
##            matching unprivileged-user behavior on Linux.
##         Bonus fixes that come along for free:
##         - PRIO_PROCESS + who != 0 now validates the target
##           pid exists (ESRCH on miss).  PRIO_PGRP / PRIO_USER
##           continue to silently succeed because we don't
##           model pgrps or per-user task sets.
##         - Out-of-range prio is silently clamped to [-20, 19]
##           matching Linux saturation semantics, instead of
##           ignoring it.
##         - rlimit_nice_check_with clamps soft to 40 before
##           the i32 subtraction, eliminating overflow risk for
##           pathologically large soft limits.
##      Coverage:
##         - getpriority(PRIO_PROCESS, 0) returns 20 (not 0).
##         - setpriority(PRIO_PROCESS, 0, 0) returns 0.
##         - setpriority(_, _, 19) returns 0 (max nice always OK).
##         - setpriority(_, _, 100) returns 0 (silent clamp).
##         - setpriority(PRIO_PROCESS, MAX_PID, _) returns ESRCH.
##         - getpriority(PRIO_PROCESS, MAX_PID) returns ESRCH.
##         - which > 2 returns EINVAL for both syscalls.
##         - rlimit_nice_check_with decision table:
##              (INF, -20) -> Ok
##              (0,   -1)  -> EACCES (floor=20)
##              (20,  -1)  -> EACCES (floor=0)
##              (21,  -1)  -> Ok      (floor=-1, == floor allowed)
##              (21,  -2)  -> EACCES (below floor)
##              (40,  -20) -> Ok      (full Linux range)
##              (1000,-20) -> Ok      (clamp to 40 prevents overflow)
##         - rlimit_nice_check_for_caller in kernel context
##           (caller_pid = None) always Ok, matching the
##           RLIMIT_AS / RLIMIT_FSIZE bypass rule.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * The 20-vs-0 return-value fix is technically a
##           behavior change, but the previous value was simply
##           wrong against Linux's documented kernel-ABI
##           contract.  Userspace programs that copy what they
##           see in real Linux would compute nice = 20 -
##           syscall_rval, which produced nice=20 here — they
##           would think they were already at the lowest
##           priority and refuse to call setpriority(-N).  The
##           new return value lets such programs see nice=0
##           (default) and decide whether to attempt a boost.
##         * Helper split (rlimit_nice_check_for_caller vs
##           _with) follows the exact pattern already used for
##           RLIMIT_FSIZE clip/check — the _with form is a pure
##           function the self-test can drive deterministically.
##      Limitation: getpriority always reports nice=0 — we
##      don't track per-process nice because the scheduler
##      doesn't honor it.  setpriority is correspondingly a
##      no-op for the scheduler; we only enforce the *policy*
##      surface so privilege-dropping programs see the correct
##      EACCES.  When real per-process nice tracking lands
##      (e.g. for the priority calculator in
##      sched::Scheduler::pick_next), wire it into the pcb's
##      Process struct and have getpriority report it.
##      Limitation: sched_setscheduler doesn't yet enforce
##      RLIMIT_RTPRIO.  Same shape of fix — accept policy 1/2
##      (FIFO/RR) only if param.sched_priority <= rlim_cur
##      (RLIMIT_RTPRIO).  Tracked for a follow-up batch.
##      Update: addressed in item 75 below.

##  75. Validate sched_param + enforce RLIMIT_RTPRIO in
##      sched_setscheduler / sched_setparam — DONE.
##      Fifteenth "upgrade a stub" batch.  Tightens the
##      policy-installation surface for Linux real-time
##      scheduling syscalls.
##         - sys_sched_setscheduler now:
##              * Tightens the policy whitelist to
##                {0,1,2,3,5,6,7}.  Policy 4 was historically
##                SCHED_ISO (rejected even on modern Linux);
